Serious Defense in Guangdong and Guangxi: Actively Expanding Military Strength. Guangxi Adds Three Divisions, Guangdong Establishes 4th and 5th Armies. Generals of the 19th Route Army are Active in Guangxi and Guangdong. 84

Guangzhou Communication: The situation in the Southwest is still not optimistic. The situation on the borders of Guangxi and Hunan and on the borders of Fujian and Guangdong is becoming increasingly serious. Therefore, at present, the Guangxi army is unusually busy with military deployments from Quanzhou to Longhuguan. They have been stockpiling military rations for days and purchasing military supplies and kerosene and electric oil worth over one million yuan from a certain place. The Guangxi army in Quanzhou is now commanded by Xia Weiyi, the commander of the 15th Army, as the forward commander. Wang Zanbin has been promoted to army commander and commands three elite divisions that can be deployed at any time. The 7th Army under Liao Lei is deployed on the Guangxi-Guizhou border. The regular Guangxi army has only five or six divisions, which is insufficient. Therefore, generals of the former 19th Route Army have recently been employed to organize anti-Japanese national salvation armies in Guangxi. It is heard that the newly formed division established by Weng Zhaoyuan in Guangxi has been established. In addition, two former division commanders of the 19th Route Army have also each organized a division, for a total of three newly formed divisions. The soldiers are all from the Guangxi provincial militia, who have received considerable training, so the anti-Japanese national salvation army is progressing very smoothly. As for Guangdong Province, the defense arrangements for the northeast river defenses are even more serious. The Second Army, which departed for Chenzhou some time ago, returned to the Guangdong border. The Fourth Division is stationed at Pingshi Lechang, the Fifth Division is deployed in Renhua, and the Sixth Division is distributed in Jiufeng, forming a parallel line, and contacting the First Division of the First Army in Nanxiong. The Chen regiment of the Second Division stationed in Ganzhou has returned to Dayu to support the various units of the Second Division in Xinfeng. The Third Division returns to Sannan, and the Seventh Division of the Third Army in Dongjiang defends Xunwu. From Xunwu to Jiaoling and Pingyuan, the Independent First Division chooses key points to garrison. The Ninth Division stationed in Chaoan has recently moved to Xingning and Dabu, and various regiments of the Guards Brigade are firmly defending the northeastern border. In order to expand military strength, the Independent First Division will be expanded into the Fourth Army. The original First and Second Brigades of the Independent First Division will be expanded into divisions, with Huang Renhuan as the commander of the Fourth Army, Zeng Youren as the commander of the Tenth Division, and Yan Yingyu as the commander of the Eleventh Division. The four regiments of the original Training Division and the Independent Second Brigade will be merged into the Fifth Army, with Miao Peinan as the commander of the Fifth Army, Tan Sui as the commander of the Thirteenth Division, and Chen Zhang as the commander of the Fourteenth Division. The above two armies are expected to be formally formed and deployed around July 1. In addition, a First Independent Brigade has recently been formed, which is reorganized from various specialized units, with Kong Kequan as the commander of the First Independent Brigade. Guangdong's military strength has increased so dramatically that it is rumored that several divisions will be transferred to the north in the future. Since the Southwest has raised the banner of the Anti-Japanese Army, it has recruited all the generals of the 19th Route Army who fought against Japan in the past. In addition to Weng Zhaoyuan and others who are active in Guangxi, Chief Commander of the former 19th Route Army Jiang Guangnai responded to the call of the authorities and arrived in Guangzhou on the 26th. He immediately discussed major plans with Li Zongren and Chen Jitang. It is heard that Jiang will assume important tasks. After Jiang stays in Guangdong for a few days to discuss matters thoroughly, he will go to Nanning to discuss important public affairs with Bai Chongxi. (June 27)

Remnant Bandits Stir Up Trouble in Northeastern Fujian; Rampant in Luoyuan and Lianjiang Counties 85

Fuzhou Dispatch: After rigorous suppression by stationed troops, remnant bandits in the counties of Chong'an, Pucheng, Jian'ou in northern Fujian and Lianjiang, Luoyuan, and Ningde in eastern Fujian had been gradually subdued. Recently, they have seized the opportunity to stir up trouble again. In northern Fujian, the band led by Huang Ligui, which had previously suffered repeated defeats by various armies and fled into Jiangxi province, has now been attacked by Jiangxi troops and is fleeing back into Fujian in an attempt to survive. A remnant force of over 300 bandits recently fled from Xiangdun to the Guangze Yangshang border, intending to join forces with the remnant bandits of Shilong, attempting to invade Chong'an and Pucheng. The troops stationed there have intensified their joint efforts to encircle the main bandit force on Yangshang. Furthermore, bandits from Shunchang, previously incited by Huang Ligui, gathered and hid in remote villages, engaging in arson and looting. Although the stationed troops had sent forces to suppress them, they have not been completely eradicated. Recently, these bandits, believing there was an opportunity to exploit, even attacked Guixi Yangdun, looting and kidnapping seven men and women. The bandit forces are quite rampant, and people from various villages are fleeing to the county seat for safety. Among them, the refugees from Guixi, Yangdun, and Renshou are particularly numerous, with a total of about 1,900 elderly, young, men, and women following the troops, temporarily retreating from Shakou to Renshou. The bandits attacked and occupied Renshou, burned down the local government office and the house of district chief Wu Shaoyi, and looted every household, creating a tragic scene. Now, Shunchang county seat is overcrowded with fleeing residents, leading to a shortage of food. The people of Shunchang have separately requested the inspection army and the provincial authorities to quickly suppress the bandits and relieve the people's suffering. The inspection army has already entered Yangkou. The number of bandits is limited and should not be difficult to annihilate. However, the losses in the three villages of Renshou, Guiyang, etc., have been significant. In eastern Fujian, the banditry in Pingnan has been rampant for the past two months. The other night, another 40 to 50 bandits advanced from the north gate area towards the northeastern rear mountains. After being discovered by the soldiers guarding the city, they immediately opened fire. The bandits then occupied the high ground in the rear mountains and returned fire. Inside the city, apart from a platoon of the security regiment, there were only a dozen or so police officers from the county government. The county magistrate then gathered over a hundred members of the militia, armed with over fifty guns, to defend the city and engage the bandits in a firefight, holding out until dawn, when the bandits began to retreat to the northeast. Currently, representatives from various public and legal organizations in the county, along with district chiefs, have decided to organize a joint anti-bandit volunteer team from eight districts. Each district will contribute twelve men, divided into two squads. In addition to thirty rifles borrowed by the county government from the provincial security bureau, the remaining weapons will be drawn from each district. The anti-bandit operation will last for three months. The minimum sustenance for the volunteer soldiers will be borne by wealthy households throughout the county. Furthermore, in the counties of Luoyuan, Lianjiang, Gutian, and Minhou, small numbers of remnant communists have been joining forces with scattered bandits in recent days, causing significant disturbances. Although local security teams and militias have been blocking them, they are difficult to suppress as they flee in one direction only to reappear in another. Among them, the losses in Luoyuan and Lianjiang counties have been particularly heavy. On the thirteenth of this month, over a hundred local communists with eighty firearms were discovered in Zhongfang Township, Fifth District, Luoyuan County. They fled from Zhengjiayang Shanglou in Ningde, aiming to promote communism, kill chiefs of the Baojia system, and kidnap people for ransom. Most of the shops owned by the Bao chiefs were burned down. On the fourteenth, they fled into Yangtou Keng, Fourth District, and sent plainclothes bandits to arrest and kill Ruan Renzhen, the former commander of a self-reformed communist guerrilla unit. On the fifteenth, the bandits fled to Wayaoban Township. The villagers, along with over twenty members of the Big Knife Society, resisted, engaging in a fierce battle for three hours. Over a dozen bandits were killed, but due to being outnumbered, five villagers were killed and two were injured. All houses in the township, totaling over a hundred households, were burned down. On the sixteenth, the bandits fled into Pubian. The county security team, led by squad leader Li, along with district chief Li of the Third District, led the militia in an ambush. County magistrate Zhang Guojian of Lianjiang personally led the security team to Pubian to assist in the suppression. The bandits occupied the high mountains and blockhouses, firing and resisting stubbornly. After a fierce battle for two hours, the bandits could not be attacked because the bridge had been destroyed. On the seventeenth, part of the bandits fled into Lanshui, and another part fled into Jianghou. On the eighteenth, they extensively looted residents' property in Yu Kou. On the nineteenth night, they fled to Liyang, and on the twentieth, they fled towards Shangling in Luoyuan Township. On the twenty-first, they fled into Shenkeng and Shekeng. On the morning of the twenty-second, they fled into Heyang. The son of the chief of the forty-eighth Bao of the area was arrested. In the afternoon, they fled to Hongyang, 25 miles away from the county seat. Currently, the banditry is very rampant. With the early rice harvest approaching, farmers cannot work in the fields, transportation is disrupted, and all industries are at a standstill. The losses throughout the county are incalculable. Yesterday, a unit dispatched by the Marine Corps was ordered to transfer to Luoyuan to suppress the bandits as soon as possible. (June 27)

Jiangxi Province Baojia Expenses Collected as Surcharges on Land Tax and Business Tax; Baojia Chiefs Can Be Prevented from Extorting and Levying Excessive Taxes, Reducing Farmers' Suffering Annually 86

Nanchang Dispatch: Baojia expenses in Jiangxi have traditionally been apportioned among households, with each household divided into four categories (A, B, C, and D) based on their wealth and collected monthly. Temporary levies such as those for blockhouses, roads, telephones, Baojia schools, conscripted labor, joint bandit suppression, and even joint security expenses are all based on the Baojia system. The apportionment methods and amounts not only differ from county to county but also vary from Jia to Jia. Taking the commonly known model county of Linchuan as an example, each able-bodied man in a household, in addition to paying the prescribed Baojia fee of over one yuan annually, faces temporary levies estimated at about two yuan. Annual conscripted labor, in addition to the prescribed service, along with temporary local mobilizations, totals over twenty days. At a minimum wage of twenty cents per day and estimated oil, salt, firewood, rice, and miscellaneous expenses of about fourteen or fifteen cents per day for each day of service, twenty days amounts to over seven yuan. Each person needs to bear ten yuan annually. However, the annual net income of even the strongest farmer is less than forty or fifty yuan, and various levies consume one-fourth or one-fifth of it. In other words, each person, in addition to their own living expenses and the burdens of the elderly and weak in their family, faces an additional pressure of one-fourth. Given the current natural disasters and man-made calamities, and the bankrupt rural economy, how can they endure it? The objective of Baojia in Jiangxi lies in the four characters of governance, education, nurturing, and defense. The character of governance has been fully implemented. Farmers, even without food for the next day, dare not owe a single penny of Baojia fees. Even carrying bran and husks as provisions for their labor service, they dare not hide and avoid their duties. The government believes that only in this way can it exert its political power. However, farmers who are bled dry and whose marrow is exhausted are about to collapse on the road, like Zhiyuan's exhausted horse. In order to improve Baojia expenses and alleviate farmers' suffering, the provincial government specially resolved at yesterday's provincial affairs meeting that Baojia expenses for the 25th year will be collected as a 20% surcharge on land tax, butchery tax, and ordinary business tax. This will be collected and disbursed by the provincial treasury. From the first of July, the collection of Baojia household fees will be suspended, and no Baojia expenses of any kind may be collected thereafter. This has been telegraphed to all commissioners and county and city governments today for compliance. After this law is implemented, farmers' suffering can be greatly reduced. Expenses will be collected through surcharges on business, butchery, and land taxes, without placing the entire burden on poor farmers. Merchants and landlords, who have a better life than farmers, can share the burden equally. Centralized collection and disbursement will reduce collection expenses. Baojia chiefs will not be able to act arbitrarily. Impoverished areas can be compensated by wealthier areas. The procedure will be simplified, eliminating the need for Baojia chiefs to constantly demand and harass people. However, Baojia malpractices will remain as in the past. For matters not regulated or mandated by superiors, Baojia chiefs can still invent various pretexts and tricks to extort money. Receiving a collection order is like receiving a sacred decree. Superiors take one, and subordinates extract many times more. Therefore, the authorities should pay close attention and prevent Baojia chiefs from arbitrarily turning things upside down and causing misery to our people. (June 25)

Guangdong Silk Industry Gradually Shows Signs of Recovery; Prices of Yarn and Silk are More Expensive Than Last Year; Exports of Raw Silk Have Also Increased 87

Guangzhou Dispatch: The silk industry in Guangdong Province has recently shown signs of recovery. Silkworm farmers are actively cultivating mulberry fields, and silk factories are resuming operations one after another. Unemployed silk reeling workers are no longer forced to wander to other places. According to old farmers in Shunde, a major silk-producing area, the slump in Guangdong silk was most severe last year. Mulberry leaves for feeding silkworms fell in price to two or three dimes per hundred catties, and no one cared. Silkworm cocoons were only worth four yuan per ten thousand shells, and mulberry seedlings were only one yuan thirty or forty cents per ten thousand plants. Whether they planted mulberries or produced silkworm eggs, they went bankrupt due to low prices. They sold their children and daughters, and moved and wandered. Almost half of the silkworm farmers in Shunde fled. This year, overseas buyers of raw silk from Guangdong Province have gradually returned to their old ways, and silk prices have risen accordingly. The withered mulberry and silkworm industry in Shunde and Nanhai has recovered. It has been found that the price of mulberry has rebounded to thirteen or fourteen yuan per hundred catties this year. Those who converted mulberry fields to grow miscellaneous grains last year have resumed planting mulberries this year. The price of silkworm cocoons has also risen accordingly, with each ten thousand shells worth over nine yuan. Dozens of silk weaving factories in Shunde and Nanhai have resumed operations. Raw silk is in high demand both domestically and internationally. As of yesterday, the price of silk from Nanhai Jiujiang was over one thousand yuan per hundred catties, and the next best was also worth over nine hundred yuan. Since resuming operations, silk products woven by yarn and silk factories have also improved. Even undyed plain silk has now risen in price to sixteen or seventeen yuan per bolt (about four or five Zhang) (it was only worth seven yuan last year), but sales are still very smooth. Many weavers are working overtime. As for the foreign sales of raw silk, in addition to exports to the United States and France, India has also purchased a lot. According to a recent survey, from May 1st to June 15th of this year, Guangzhou transported 800 catties of raw silk to the United States, 20,000 catties to various European countries, and 179,680 catties to Asia and India, totaling 219,360 catties, an increase of 68,000 catties compared to the same period last year. (June 27)

Shops in Jiangzhuang Town, Songjiang, Robbed 88

This is not the first time that Jiangzhuang Town in southern Pudong has been robbed. The shops are bearing the brunt of the suffering and are always vigilant. Two robbers stood guard, each carrying a handgun, flashlight, and dagger as weapons. They searched and looted for about half an hour, taking a gold ring weighing five Fen, twenty-nine thousand copper coins, over fifty Jiao in paper money, six pieces of clothing, and a suitcase. Zhu Ziqin's grandson, Liangjie, suffered a knife wound to his left hand, bleeding profusely. The robbers then fled south with their loot, leaving behind a dagger. The victim has reported the incident to the Ninth Police Station for investigation.

The Provincial Government believes that the Commissioner's Offices in various places have always used the name of the county where they are stationed as the name of the Administrative Inspector Commissioner of a certain district, while the Security Commander of the district concurrently held is named with a number, which is not uniform, and documents are very inconvenient. It has been proposed to change the Commissioner's Office based on the number of the Security Commander concurrently held. The proposal was approved by the Executive Yuan and forwarded for compliance. The Security Commander of this district is the Third District, which will be corrected to the Administrative Inspector Commissioner's Office of the Third District. Commissioner Wang, after receiving the order, has decided to make the correction from July 1st and has instructed all counties to take note.

Wuxi: Business Tax Bureau Chief Steals Electricity 91

Zhou Yulin, Chief of the Liyang County Business Tax Bureau, privately connected electric lights in the Liyang Tax Bureau in January of last year and stole electricity. He was caught by the Zhenheng Electric Light Factory of the county, which sent personnel to join the Chief of the First Police Station in the public security department for investigation. The factory then filed a lawsuit against Zhou Yulin for theft with the Liyang County Government, which also handled judicial matters. After trial by the county magistrate Chen Fu, the defendant was acquitted due to insufficient evidence of guilt. The factory was not satisfied and appealed to the local District Court. The court rejected the appeal and upheld the original judgment. The factory was still unwilling to accept the judgment and continued to appeal to the High Court. After reviewing the case, the High Court considered the appeal to be justified and sent it back to the local court for retrial. After several trials by Judge Liu, the judgment was announced yesterday: Zhou Yulin, with the intention of unlawful gain, stole the property of others and was fined fifty yuan. If he is unable to pay after forced execution, he will serve one day of labor for every two yuan.

Stolen Coal Shipped to Chengjiang and Unloaded Secretly 92

The thirteen ships of stolen coal from Liujiang were shipped to Wuxi, but due to accusations and sanctions from all sides, they could not be unloaded, as detailed in previous reports. The stolen coal was recently shipped to Jiangyin. According to news from Jiangyin, someone witnessed that the coal was not shipped to Shanghai. After the ships entered the Yingtian River at the south gate, the coal boss directed the unloading of the coal at night. However, where the coal was unloaded is still unknown. The reason why the smugglers claimed that they had shipped the stolen coal to Shanghai was to avoid the attention of the people of Wuxi and Jiangyin.

Preventing Tea Levies in Rural Areas 93

The Tea House Trade Association of this city reported that members in rural areas have reported that recently, individuals posing as officials of micro-tax collection agencies have been surveying tea counters in various shops and collecting tea house levies. They have requested relief. It was pointed out that the county's budget for the 25th year has been approved by the Provincial Government Committee, and the tea house levies have been reduced by 186 yuan compared to last year. How can these officials start collecting levies in rural areas where they have never been collected before? This is clearly exceeding the budget and collecting taxes outside the law, violating the orders of the Ministry and the Province. Therefore, the sixteenth executive committee meeting was convened yesterday and resolved not to assume the obligation of paying taxes and to petition the relevant ministries and departments of the Central Government and the Provincial Government to quickly stop this practice and punish them according to law. As for the tea house management licenses, which are due for renewal, they should be collected and transferred to the respective branch bureau chiefs for renewal according to the practice of last year.

Seven-Month-Old Infant Killed 94

Gao Quanrong, a villager from Gaoxiang Shang, about two li from Sitou Town in this county, died of illness in January of this year, leaving behind his wife, Lin, who is thirty years old, and two sons. The eldest, Bingrong, is four years old, and the youngest, Bingquan, is only seven months old. The day before yesterday afternoon, Lin, driven by the need to make a living, went to work in the fields, often leaving her young son sleeping in a cradle at home. When the sun was setting, Lin finished her work and returned home to prepare to breastfeed, but the child was nowhere to be found. After searching everywhere without success, at around 7 PM, she found the child in the Qingshui Pit near the back door. He had already died. Lin was heartbroken upon seeing this. However, the matter was strange, and it may have been a murder.

Nanhui: Squad Member Murders in Jealousy 95

Dai Keming, a squad member of the 14th Security Battalion stationed in this city, and his wife, Gu, rented a house in the Chen residence at the south gate. Dai's comrade in arms often visited his house for leisure. Yesterday morning, Dai returned home after being relieved from his post at the county government gate and saw his wife and a man lying in a pool of blood. Upon inspection, his wife had been shot once in the head, arm, and chest, and the man had been shot once in the waist, all fatal. Dai immediately reported to the battalion. The battalion investigated and found that the man was Jin Yayu, also a squad member of the battalion and Dai's comrade in arms, who often visited his house. The county government dispatched a coroner from the trial division, Liang, for inspection. The results showed that the woman's body was indeed murdered, and the man's body was a suicide. It is rumored that the reason for the tragic murder was caused by jealousy.

Pinghu: Electrocution Kills Two 100

The Meihua Barber Shop in Houchai, outside the East Gate, recently installed a flour mill motor. The shop assistants were not familiar with its use. Suddenly, there was an electrical leak. The customer was startled and jumped up, running out the door. The shop assistant, Ah Ti, was sucked in by the electricity, his legs flailing wildly, suffering severe burns. On the same day (28th), Shi Guohou, a 20-year-old apprentice carpenter at the East Gate Kou Lime Wood Shop, was tricked by someone who told him to climb to the top of the electric pole on the city wall. Shi Jia showed off his bravery, climbed up like a monkey, and when he was about to reach the top of the pole, he grabbed a bare electric wire for assistance. As soon as he made contact, sparks burst out, and he lost control, falling from the top of the pole onto the city wall and then rolling from the city wall to the ground. When he fell from the pole, his body was parallel to the electric pole. The middle of the pole was nailed with sharp nails, causing deep nail wounds to his neck and abdomen. Blood gushed out like a spring. His brother rushed to the scene upon hearing the news and hired someone to carry him quickly to the hospital. The hospital refused to accept him because his teeth had fallen out and his brain had cracked. He was carried back and died immediately.

Local News

New French Ambassador Mr. Noulens Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Morning; Reception for Chinese and Foreign Communities at 4 PM Today; Presentation of Credentials Set for the 4th or 6th of Next Month 105

Mr. Noulens, the newly appointed French ambassador to China, arrived in China on the 29th of last month aboard the French ship "Felix Roussel" from Marseille to assume his new post. After passing through Annam, he disembarked to meet with the Governor-General of Annam, and then took the same ship to Hong Kong and then to Shanghai. He entered the port at around 7 a.m. yesterday and arrived at the northern dock of the China Merchants Bureau at 8 a.m. People from all walks of life who came to the port to welcome him included: Mr. Geng Jiaji, representing Mayor Wu; Mr. Zhao Tiezhang, Deputy Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs; Mr. Zhang Mengling; Mr. Yang Hu, Commander of the Songhu Garrison; Secretaries Wang Zhinan and Sun Liping; Central Committee members Li Shizeng and Chu Minyi; Mr. Qian Xinzhi from the banking industry; Mr. Du Yuesheng, etc. On the French side, those present included: Chargé d'affaires Mr. Hobernot; Commercial Counselor Mr. Sachet; Consul General in Shanghai Mr. Bodard; Military Commander in Shanghai Mr. Berti; Commissioner of the French Concession Police Mr. Fabre; and more than 300 representatives of the French community.

Disembarkation and Military Review

Ambassador Noulens shook hands with each of the welcoming personnel to express his gratitude. At 9 a.m., he boarded a special reception boat and went directly to the Bund Wharf on French Avenue to disembark. At that time, a part of the Chinese and French welcoming personnel had already been waiting at the wharf. The French side specially dispatched French troops stationed in Shanghai and armed French and Annamese police, leading a tank convoy, a motorcycle convoy, and a military band, to form a line from the Bund on French Avenue to the Bund on Avenue Edward VII. The traffic on that section of the road was completely cut off from dawn until 9:30 a.m., and pedestrians had to take a detour. After Ambassador Noulens disembarked, the military band played the French national anthem and held a military review ceremony, and then he returned to the French Consulate General to rest. Full photo of the French Ambassador with welcomers (International News Agency report).

Statement from Havas News Agency, Shanghai: After disembarking, Ambassador Noulens went to the consulate to attend a reception and delivered a brief speech, saying that he was very happy to be appointed as ambassador and come to the new China, to be able to reunite with old friends and make new ones. He said that he had already gained a understanding of China during his tenure as consul in Kunming and consul general in Shanghai. This time he will work with the same enthusiasm with the Chinese government and French people to further strengthen the friendship between China and France, and will also sincerely cooperate with people from all countries. Ambassador Noulens may go to Nanjing next month on the 4th to meet with Chairman Lin of the National Government to present his credentials.

Brief Biography

Ambassador Noulens is of medium height and full of energy. When he arrived in Shanghai, he was wearing a gray-black suit, rimless glasses, and black leather shoes. His attitude was very amiable. Ambassador Noulens is a bachelor, so he did not bring a wife or entourage with him. He is 52 years old and started in the diplomatic service in 1908. He first came to China in 1912 as a consul in Shanghai, and then served as acting consul general. Later, he resigned and returned to China. In 1927, he came to China again as consul general in Shanghai. Two years later, he was transferred back to China and served as an assistant in the Marine Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and then promoted to Director of the Oriental Department. Later, he served as Minister to Yugoslavia, and then transferred to Minister to Czechoslovakia. Just when the Sino-French envoys were being upgraded, the former Minister to China, Mr. Zhang Lideng, died in Beijing. Therefore, the country appointed Mr. Noulens as the first ambassador to China. Because he has lived in China for many years, he is very familiar with the situation in our country and has a harmonious relationship with the people of our country. The increase in the number of Chinese directors in the Shanghai French Concession Public Works Department, and the execution of duties by Chinese lawyers in the French Concession, were all realized during Mr. Noulens' tenure as consul general in Shanghai.

Various Social Engagements

Mr. Noulens will host a reception for Chinese and foreign communities in Shanghai at the Consulate General at 4 p.m. today. Mr. Li Shizeng, a member of the Central Committee, will also host a banquet at the World Academic Society on Fooking Road at 7 p.m. today to welcome Mr. Noulens, and invite celebrities from all walks of life to accompany him. At 8 p.m., the Sino-French Friendship Association will also hold a tea party at the World Academic Society to welcome him. It is also reported that the members of the Sino-French Friendship Association in Nanjing will host a banquet to welcome him one day after the ambassador presents his credentials.

The Money Trade Association Passed a Major Resolution Yesterday: Cancel the Cash-on-Delivery Fund; All Industry Cash-on-Delivery Money to be Settled Daily in the Vault; Implementation Today with the Return of 30,000 per Establishment 106

The Shanghai Money Trade Association held its ninth member representative meeting of the third session yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. In addition to deciding on the interest rate for June, it also resolved to cancel the cash-on-delivery fund and return it, replacing it with a settlement by the reserve vault. Forty-six representatives from Fu Yuan, Zhi Yu, Yi Da, Hong Sheng, Zi Feng, Fu Kang, Run, Wu Feng, An Kang, Hong Xiang, Shen Yuan, Dun Yu, Tong Yu, and other establishments, including Zhang Mengzhou, Chen Wenqing, Ye Xiuchun, Zhao Songyuan, and others, totaling eighty-six people attended.

Reports: Chairman Shao Yanshan reported: Minutes of the previous meeting; Documents received and sent in June: 36 documents received and 438 documents sent; Industry gatherings held at the association eight times in June; The Shanghai North Nursing Home's summer epidemic prevention center will be handled as decided at the 17th executive committee meeting. The donation amount will still follow the old practice: member establishments in the northern Shanghai area will donate 50 yuan in national currency per establishment, and Yuanzi establishments will donate half. The clinic is scheduled to open on July 1st; Various reports regarding the reserve vault.

Discussion Items: Discussions then began on: June interest rate, please vote on the proposal. Resolved: 2.595%; According to a letter from member Yong Yu Sheng Ji Zhuang, the manager, Mr. Xie Taofu, passed away on June 11th. After a shareholder meeting, it was resolved to promote Mr. Wang Zhongshu to manager. This was submitted to the 18th executive committee meeting of the third session for review and deemed qualified. It was then submitted for a decision in accordance with regulations. Resolved: Approved; Approve the proposal from the 17th executive committee of the third session to cancel and return the cash-on-delivery fund of 30,000 yuan in national currency per establishment deposited by member establishments, and to have all industry cash-on-delivery amounts settled daily with the reserve vault. Is this feasible? Please vote on the proposal. Resolved: Approved. A special request is made to ratify the resolution. Resolved: Approved. Implemented starting June 30th.

Cash-on-Delivery Fund: The Huiliu General Association of the Money Trade Association has existed for a long time. Before the establishment of the Shanghai Bank Clearing House, it was the only clearing house for negotiable instruments in Shanghai. It stipulated that payments between industry members above 500 yuan must obtain an official bill and be totaled at the general association that evening. Most relied on the general association to collect payment. For balances below 500 yuan, there was no need to deliver cash. That is, each establishment contributed 30,000 yuan and handed it over to the Money Trade Joint Reserve Vault, called the "Cash-on-Delivery Fund", for safekeeping, and settled mutually at the end of each year. Now the Money Trade has decided to cancel the cash-on-delivery fund and settle directly with the Money Trade Reserve Vault every night. Yesterday, the member representative meeting approved the implementation starting today and has notified all member establishments to comply.

Various Banks Pay in: Savings Reserve Fund; Central Trust Bureau Also Ordered to Pay 107

The Ministry of Finance levies a savings bank guarantee reserve fund, specially stored to protect the legal rights of the people. Every six months, each bank pays in one-quarter of the total savings amount calculated for the half-year. Now is the half-year settlement period, and the Ministry of Finance has ordered all banks to handle it. The Central Savings Association, run by the Central Trust Bureau, has also received this order and will pay in one-quarter of the total deposit base.

Ma Liang Requests: Concession Tobacco Prohibition Steps; Reporting Coolie Smokers to Hospital for Rehabilitation; Second Phase Licenses to Expire Today 108

The second phase of smoker licenses for the Municipal Public Security Bureau will expire today. Smokers who have belatedly registered during the reporting period are extremely enthusiastic. Mr. Ma Liang, the special commissioner for reporting in Shanghai, went to Beijing to report to the authorities on the prohibition of tobacco in the concessions and to request instructions. The details are as follows:

Second Phase Licenses to Expire Tomorrow

The second phase of smoker licenses, issued by the Municipal Public Security Bureau starting April 1st, was originally scheduled to expire on May 31st. However, because there were not many license renewals within the deadline, to give smokers a reasonable amount of time, the deadline was extended by one month to the end of June. In total, more than 21,000 people renewed their licenses. Compared to the original number of registered license holders, there is still a difference of more than 10,000 people. However, the bureau will not extend the second phase of licenses again and has decided that today is the last day. Each district will extend the hours to 7 p.m. After that, license renewals will be closed.

Sending Coolie Smokers for Rehabilitation

Since the Municipal Public Security Bureau started the general reporting work of smokers on May 10th, the reporting period will end on August 10th. As of the day before yesterday, a total of more than 6,500 smokers in the city who had not registered and obtained licenses had belatedly registered. Most of them are coolie smokers, and in fact, it is difficult for them to obtain a license and smoke. If they go to the hospital for rehabilitation, they will not have the money to pay for it. Therefore, the bureau will issue certificates to them separately and designate nearby hospitals in the smokers' locations for free rehabilitation. According to the statistics of various hospitals, more than 2,000 coolies have successfully quit their addiction.

Requesting Instructions on Concession Tobacco Prohibition in Beijing

Regarding the prohibition of drugs and tobacco in the concessions, although the Military Affairs Commission's General Supervision Department has separately instructed the Shanghai Municipal Government and the Commissioner's Office, according to the Dagong News Agency reporter, the implementation methods have been discussed by the authorities several times. However, negotiations have not yet been formally submitted to the concession authorities. Therefore, it is expected that the implementation on July 1st will not achieve its goals. Mr. Ma Liang, the special commissioner stationed in Shanghai, went to Beijing on the evening of the 28th to report on the situation of tobacco prohibition in Shanghai to the General Supervision Department and other agencies, and to request instructions on various implementation methods such as tobacco prohibition in the concessions.

The Greater America Evening News reports that the US Embassy in China will move from Beijing to the capital in August. The US Ambassador will be stationed in the capital for a longer period of time than now. Johnson was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai from Beijing today, but it is now known that he will arrive tomorrow morning. Ministry of Railways Mortgages Loan from Agricultural Bank of China: 3 Million Yuan Contract Signed; For the Construction of the Sichuan-Hunan and Sichuan-Guizhou Railways; Term Set for One Year at 8% Interest 113

The Ministry of Railways mortgaged a loan of 3 million yuan to the Farmers Bank of China with the third phase of railway construction bonds for the construction of the Sichuan-Hunan and Sichuan-Guizhou railways. A contract has been successfully signed. The details are as follows:

Construction of the Sichuan-Hunan and Sichuan-Guizhou Railways

The Ministry of Railways issued 120 million yuan of the third phase of railway construction bonds, to be issued in three phases over three years, with 40 million yuan each time. The first issue was on March 1st. Now, to build the two major railways of Sichuan-Hunan and Sichuan-Guizhou, it has mortgaged 3 million yuan to the Farmers Bank of China. This has been agreed upon by Zhang Gongquan, Minister of Railways, and Zhu Runsheng, manager of the Shanghai branch of the Farmers Bank of China. 4 million yuan of the third phase of railway bonds will be mortgaged for 3 million yuan, with a term of one year and an interest rate of 8%.

3 Million Yuan Contract Signed

After the draft loan contract was drawn up, it was approved by the Ministry of Railways and approved by the Hankou head office of the Farmers Bank of China. The formal contract was signed in Shanghai. Although the term is set for one year, the contract states that it may be temporarily withdrawn from the Farmers Bank of China as needed for the project. It is reported that after the Ministry of Railways successfully borrowed the money, it has begun construction of the Sichuan-Hunan and Sichuan-Guizhou railways. Construction will begin as soon as the survey is completed.

Jianghai Customs Proclaims Revised Rules for Rewarding Informants of Smuggled Goods by Ministry of Finance; Informant Boxes Set Up in Various Places for Merchants to Submit Letters; Jianghai Customs Has Been Ordered to Proclaim to Inform Merchants 114

Tang Haian, Superintendent of Jianghai Customs, and Parson, Tax Officer, respectively issued a bulletin after receiving an order from the Ministry of Finance to revise the reward method for informing and rewarding seized smuggled goods.

Order to Revise the Reward Method

Jianghai Customs Bulletin No. 1524 states: According to the order of the Ministry of Finance, in order to promote customs anti-smuggling and encourage informant, the reward method is now revised as follows: An informant box will be set up in the customs and its branches and sub-cards, allowing ordinary merchants to submit letters informing about smuggling, sales, and possession. In addition to stating the specific facts of smuggling, sales, and possession, and the names and addresses of the perpetrators or shops and factories, the informant must also provide his name and address. The customs branches and sub-cards will absolutely keep the name of the informant secret. In addition to submitting letters, the informant may also go to the customs branches and sub-cards or local military police to inform verbally, as usual. If there is no informant box nearby, the informant may notify the customs card by telegram or mail. The informant documents will be opened and reviewed personally by the person in charge of the customs or branch card. When necessary, the informant may be invited to inquire secretly, or go to the designated location to investigate and seize smuggled goods. Those who have obtained smuggled goods as a result of informant will be rewarded in accordance with the newly established rewarding rules to the informant after the card is processed. It should be proclaimed that all know, etc. Therefore, it should be followed. All merchants, etc. should know, hereby proclaim.

Reward Method for Seizing Smuggled Goods

Jianghai Customs Bulletin No. 1525 states: According to the order of the Ministry of Finance, the reward method for seizing smuggled goods is now revised as follows: Those who inform as an informant and seize smuggled goods will be given 50% of the proceeds of the penalty after the card has been disposed of. All agencies and military police (including road police) who seize smuggled goods and transfer them to the customs for processing will be given 50% of the proceeds from the disposal after the card is processed. Business partners or factory partners who report smuggling or sales of their own business or factory, and the customs seizes smuggled goods as a result, the reporter will be given 50% of the proceeds from the card being disposed of. The customs investigates and seizes smuggled goods, such as those who invite the military police (including the road police) to assist on the spot, will be given 10% of the bonus to the assisting military police. It should be proclaimed that all should know, etc. Therefore, all military police merchants and people know, hereby proclaim.

Impact of Smuggling on General Commodity Prices: Announcement by the National Tariff Commission of the Ministry of Finance 115

According to an announcement by the National Tariff Commission of the Ministry of Finance, the wholesale export, import, and cost of living indices for Shanghai in May of the 25th year (of the Republic, i.e., 1936) all showed a slight decline compared to the previous month. The largest decline was in exports, at 2.9%, followed by wholesale prices at 1.4%. The declines in imports and the cost of living were more moderate, both below 0.5%. In recent months, smuggling in North China has become increasingly rampant. The types of smuggled goods, initially limited to artificial silk, sugar, and cigarette paper, have now spread to seafood, woolens, cotton cloth, flour, kerosene, gasoline, and various sundry goods. The sale of smuggled goods, initially confined to North China, is now encroaching on Central China. The decline in commodity prices this month is likely related to smuggling. It is hoped that the government's recent measures to investigate the transportation and sale of imported goods will be effective in preventing smuggling. Otherwise, there is a possibility that general commodity prices will continue to fall.

Wholesale Price Index: The general index was 105.8, a decrease of 1.4% compared to 107.3 last month, and an increase of 11.4% compared to 95.0 in the same month last year. In the full table, prices of 21 items increased, prices of 78 items decreased, and prices of 55 items remained unchanged. Compared to the previous month, all eight category indices showed a slight decline except for a slight increase in miscellaneous items. The largest declines were in food, textiles, metals, and chemicals. The other three categories all had declines of less than 0.8%. The food category index was 91.5, a decrease of 3.6% compared to 94.9 last month. The price of white rice decreased due to a large amount of Yangke Xian rice in stock and sluggish smuggling, while hoarders sold off stock due to the approaching mold season. The price of wheat decreased due to sluggish flour sales and the expectation of a good harvest in Jiangsu and Shandong. The price of soybeans decreased due to falling prices reported in Dalian and sluggish sales. The customs price uniformly depreciated. The sales of flour in Tianjin were affected by smuggling, but the price did not fall much due to cost factors. The textile and raw materials category index was 86.6, a decrease of 2.4% compared to 88.7 last month. The prices of artificial silk and cotton cloth both tended to weaken due to the impact of smuggling. The export of white silk was already sluggish, and recently, overseas Japanese silk was sold at a discount, so the selling price slightly decreased. The price of cotton fell along with silk and crepe because the market repeatedly spread rumors that the United States and China would establish cotton and wheat loans, and the sales of cloth were also depressed. The metal category index was 126.8, a decrease of 1.6% compared to 128.8 last month, due to sluggish sales and falling prices of lead and tin. In the chemical category, the index fell from 140.5 last month to 138.2 this month, a decrease of 1.6%, due to a sharp drop in the market price of Qingguangyuan and weakening prices of soda ash, alum, and paraffin. (Shenshi News Agency)

Export Price Index: The general index was 94.5, a decrease of 2.9% compared to 97.3 last month, and an increase of 26.0% compared to 75.0 in the same month last year. In the full table, prices of 12 items increased, prices of 37 items decreased, and prices of 17 items remained unchanged. All three category indices showed a uniform decline compared to the previous month. The index of raw materials was 83.6, a decrease of 3.7% compared to 86.8 last month. The export of white tung oil was sluggish, and the domestic sales of raw oil and asphalt were depressed. The prices of cotton yarn and white ash from ash factories uniformly depreciated. The raw materials index was 108.6, a decrease of 2.9% compared to 111.9 last month. Pure antimony, peanuts, and raw kernels all reported falling prices in the place of origin due to ample inventory. Ramie weakened because the new season was approaching and exports were sluggish. Other items, such as wheat, green beans, cotton, and Jian pine wood, also showed price declines. The consumer goods index was 77.0, a decrease of 1.3% compared to 78.0 last month. Flour and coarse cloth were affected by smuggling. The price of eggs fell, along with egg whites, Longkou vermicelli, and Huzhou silk crepe, due to seasonal factors.

Import Price Index: The general index was 140.3, a decrease of 0.4% compared to 140.9 last month, and an increase of 13.2% compared to 123.9 in the same month last year. In the full table, prices of 10 items increased, prices of 30 items decreased, and prices of 42 items remained unchanged. Compared to the previous month, the raw materials index slightly increased, while the consumer goods and raw materials indices slightly decreased. The raw materials index was 133.2, an increase of 1.0% compared to 131.9 last month. The prices of most items decreased, but the price of American cotton, which has the largest weight, increased in foreign markets due to the passage of the Smith-Connally Act in the United States, contrary to the trend of local cotton, so the market price was still higher than last month. Copper ingots and white coal also tended to be firm, so the category index slightly increased. The consumer goods index was 140.9, a decrease of 1.1% compared to 142.4 last month. Red and white sugar and flour were affected by smuggling and had sluggish sales, but the price did not fall much. Yangke rice, Yuan Yu silk, and fresh oranges also decreased in price. The raw materials index was 148.6, a decrease of 0.4% compared to 149.2 last month. The market price of artificial silk fell from 195 yuan per hundred pounds last month to 185 yuan this month due to the customs auction of large quantities of confiscated smuggled goods. Other items, such as fine foreign cloth, plain white iron, cut iron, soda ash, caustic soda, Qingguangyuan, writing paper, kraft paper, and coconut oil, also showed weakness.

Cost of Living Index: The general index was 111.1, a decrease of 0.5% compared to 111.7 last month, and an increase of 5.2% compared to 105.6 in the same month last year. In the full table, prices of 9 items increased, prices of 11 items decreased, and prices of 23 items remained unchanged. Compared to the previous month, all five category indices showed a slight decline except for a slight increase in miscellaneous items. The food category index was 97.6, a decrease of 0.3% compared to 97.9 last month. Radishes, scallions, and tomatoes increased sharply, and pork and soybean oil tended to rise, but green vegetables and pickles suddenly fell sharply. The retail price of white rice, the most important item, also fell along with the wholesale price. The clothing index was 84.2, a decrease of 0.1% compared to 84.3 last month, due to the weakening sales price of cotton Zhigong cloth. The rent index fell from 110.3 last month to 109.6 this month, a decrease of 0.6%, as a result of recent surveys showing rent reductions in the eastern and northern districts of Shanghai. The price increases and decreases in the fuel and miscellaneous categories were both small. The former index was 127.2, a decrease of 4.0% compared to 132.5 last month, and the latter index was 154.9, an increase of 0.3% compared to 154.4 last month. The main reasons for the former were the price decrease of firewood, and for the latter, the slight increase in the selling price of soap. Shenshi News Agency

South China Tea Disappears from Northeast Imports 122

Entirely Monopolized by Taiwanese Tea

The consumption of tea in various parts of Northeast China is approximately 7 million to 10 million catties per year. Before the September 18th Incident (Mukden Incident), all tea was supplied by South China. After that, Japanese merchants engaged in the tea business initially shipped 500,000 catties of Taiwanese tea to Northeast China as samples. The following year, they shipped more than 1.6 million catties. In the past two years, under the control of the Japanese, the tea market in Northeast China has been entirely replaced by Taiwanese tea. The Japanese have also heavily promoted how exquisite and inexpensive Taiwanese tea is, thus opening up new territory in the Northeast. In addition, the Japanese have requested a reduction in tariffs on Taiwanese tea. The puppet government stipulated a tea tax plus additional tax totaling 55%. For example, if the tax standard price for Taiwanese tea is 58 yuan, the standard for Chinese South China tea is 77.5 yuan. The Japanese believe that the current difference of only 19.5 yuan is not enough. They must further increase the tariff rate on South China tea and reduce the tariff rate on Taiwanese tea in order to completely eliminate South China tea from the Northeast market. Currently, the puppet government will allow the Japanese request to reduce the new tax rate on Taiwanese tea.

Polish Community in Shanghai Celebrates Maritime Day 126

Polish Embassy Closed for One Day

June 29th is Polish Maritime Day. The Polish Community Committee in Shanghai held a grand celebration on the evening of that day. The Polish Embassy and Consulate also closed for one day on this day. Maritime Day was initiated by the Polish Maritime Overseas Association and supported by the whole country. Since 1932, it has been formally designated as this day every year. In the Polish port of Gdynia, representatives from various places gather to celebrate. Last year, more than 100,000 people attended, and three things were decided: 1. The whole country jointly raised funds to build the Navy National Defense Fund; 2. The youth of the whole country should devote themselves to serving the maritime interests of Poland; 3. Actively expand the maritime significance. The port is considered one of the country's most successful construction projects. Before the port was built, Poland's overseas trade relied on the port of Wuze for transportation. From 1923, the port of Gdynia was developed with all its strength, costing a total of 500 million yuan. It is now the largest commercial port on the Baltic coast. The Polish government and the public are all proud of this, so the military must hold Maritime Day there.

Banking and Money Trade Associations Ordered to Supervise the Dismissal of Liquidation Commissioners 128

Creditors to Apply to the Court According to the Bankruptcy Law; Directors and Supervisors of Savings Deposits to be Jointly and Severally Liable for Repayment

The New Sound News Agency reports that the Shanghai Banking and Money Trade Associations received an order from the Ministry of Finance yesterday stating: "Upon investigation, in June of last year, this Ministry promulgated six measures for supervising and liquidating the banking and money house industries, dispatched commissioners to supervise and liquidate, and set a deadline of three months for completing the liquidation. The original intention was to urge the banks and money houses that had suspended operations to complete the liquidation as soon as possible and protect the interests of both debtors and creditors. Later, the liquidators and supervisors repeatedly reported the difficulties in the liquidation. This Ministry repeatedly approved extensions until the end of June this year. Now that the extension period is about to expire, the Bankruptcy Law has also been promulgated and implemented. The liquidation method stipulated in that law is more complete than the previous Provisional Regulations on the Liquidation of Merchant Debts. The local courts have a basis for handling these liquidation cases, and the progress has been quite effective. All supervisors and liquidation commissioners dispatched to the various banks and money houses should be dismissed uniformly at the end of June. The liquidation affairs should be handled by the various banks and money houses and their creditors themselves in accordance with the provisions of the Bankruptcy Law, applying to the local district court for supervision. As for savings deposits that have not yet been fully repaid, the directors and supervisors of the respective banks should be jointly and severally liable for repayment in full within this year's July, and no further delay should be allowed. In addition to separate orders, this order is hereby issued to the association for compliance."

Book Sellers Host Press Yesterday 130

Wang Longchao Reports on the Truth about Opposing Price Increases by Bookstores

The Hongwen, Nanxin, Jianshe, Bolan, Suxin and other bookstores in this city, because major bookstores are scheduled to increase book discounts from the 1st of next month, which has a significant impact on the future of their business, in addition to unanimously expressing their opposition, also hosted the press at Dalian Restaurant in Zhengjia Muqiao at 3:00 PM yesterday to report the truth about the matter. More than 20 reporters from various newspapers attended and were cordially received by Wang Longchao and other representatives of the industry. After being seated, Mr. Wang reported, saying that the bookstores in this city are divided into two types: publishing and selling, that is, the difference between large and small firms. There are more than 100 small firms in the city. The books of the major firms originally had a 60% to 70% discount, but later, because the major firms gave preferential treatment to various schools, the discounts on the books were arbitrarily reduced, which greatly affected the business of the small firms. Therefore, they had to reluctantly sacrifice and reduce the selling price to maintain their livelihoods. Unexpectedly, the major firms are now using the excuse that the discounts of the small firms are too rampant and are using the name of unifying the book price to actually increase the discounts and reduce the commission of the small firms to 20%. Each store believes that once this matter is realized, it will have a major impact on the future of their business. In addition to actively forming a trade association of booksellers, they will also argue with the major firms on the basis of reason and hope that the press will provide righteous assistance, etc. After the speech, tea and snacks were served and the meeting adjourned.

Record of the Lake Society's General Meeting of Members the Other Day: Thirteen Motions Passed, and Executive and Supervisory Committee Members Elected 132

National Federation of Commerce Cables the Ministry of Finance: Kiln Owners' Payment Slips Exempt from Stamp Duty 133

Because They are Part of the Porcelain Payment Process, Not Comparable to Invoices for Completed Sales

The Industrial Association reports that the National Federation of Commerce yesterday cabled the Ministry of Finance, stating: "We have recently received a letter from the Jingdezhen Chamber of Commerce in Jiangxi Province, which states: 'To the esteemed recipient, according to a letter from the Nine Kilns Association of this town, the procedures for buying and selling porcelain in Jingdezhen have special circumstances and differ from ordinary transactions. In ordinary transactions, customers come to the door, and the value of the goods can be decided on the spot. Once the transaction is completed, a list of the goods' value is prepared, stamps are affixed, and given to the customer, without further complications. However, the sale of porcelain is completely different. First, porcelain merchants or brokers negotiate prices on the street, and then the porcelain merchant sends a porter to the kiln owner to arrange for the loading of goods in baskets by a certain date. The kiln owner issues a payment slip to the porter who carries the porcelain. The payment slip is merely a procedure for counting the porcelain during the loading process and should not be considered a confirmation of the sale. According to the custom of selling porcelain, after the porcelain is loaded and arrives at the shop, the workers sort and select the porcelain. Sometimes five or six out of ten are kept, while other times six or seven out of ten are returned. After the sorting workers prepare a list of the actual goods received, it is sent to the kiln owner as a basis for future settlement. For example, if 100 pieces of porcelain are loaded, only 50 pieces may be sold. Therefore, the nature of the payment slip is merely a procedure in the process of selling porcelain. Moreover, the porcelain being purchased is loaded into the shop gradually, not all at once. The price of the porcelain is not listed on the payment slip, only the number of pieces. Only after all the porcelain is loaded will the previous porcelain slips be calculated, and the actual amount received and the price in foreign currency will be listed on a settlement sheet for final payment. Only then is the transaction completed. The settlement sheet should, of course, have stamps affixed, but the payment slip should be exempt. If the payment slip also requires stamps, then the same porcelain is taxed both on the goods and on the price, which is double taxation. The declining porcelain industry can hardly bear this double burden. Moreover, porcelain is a unique product of our country, and the government is enthusiastically promoting it. How can it bear to destroy it? Items such as kiln industry white clay, which are related to porcelain production, are generally exempt from taxes. This payment slip is not a formal transaction, so it should be exempt from stamp duty to show compassion. We sincerely request that you forward this to the Ministry of Finance for approval of the exemption. We are deeply grateful.' Furthermore, the Porcelain Red Shop Trade Association also sent a letter with the same content, among other things, to the association. After reviewing the payment slips issued by the kiln owners in this town, we found that they are a kind of payment process and not comparable to invoices for completed transactions. If stamps are required, not only will the procedure be cumbersome, but it will also inevitably lead to a heavy tax burden, which the merchants can hardly bear. The points mentioned are indeed the actual situation, and our association can vouch for them. May we be allowed to forward this to you to request approval of the exemption? We would be extremely grateful. Etc., as approved. It is reasonable to cable your ministry for review and approval, requesting that the payment slips issued by the kiln owners be exempt from stamp duty to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. We are deeply earnest. Respectfully, Wen Lanting, Acting Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce of the Republic of China, kowtows. Printed."

And New Freight Rates Have Been Set

Instruction of Political Prisoners in Prison to Be Implemented in Groups Starting Tomorrow 142

The Period is Set for Three Months, Ending at the End of September; Instruction Methods Divided into Group and Individual Types

The municipal party headquarters, in order to educate political prisoners in various district prisons in this city and correct their thinking, has specially organized a political prisoner instruction committee, appointing 27 people, including Pan Gongzhan, Tong Hangbai, Jiang Huaishu, and Lu Jingshi, as committee members. The group instruction will be implemented starting tomorrow (July 1st) for a period of three months. Details are noted below:

Group Instruction to Begin Tomorrow: There are a total of 103 political prisoners detained in various district prisons in this city, including 97 men and women in Jiangsu Second Prison, 4 men and women in the French Concession Special District Prison, and 2 female prisoners in the British Concession Special District Prison. Among them, there are 9 female prisoners. The committee has conducted investigations and organized the prisoners into groups for instruction based on their level of education: 4 with university degrees are formed into one group, 17 with secondary school degrees are formed into one group, 7 with primary school degrees are formed into one group, 2 civil servants are formed into one group, 15 small business owners are formed into two groups, 4 farmers are formed into one group, 39 workers are formed into four groups, and 9 unemployed are formed into one group. All of the above are in Jiangsu Second Prison. The 3 male prisoners and 1 female prisoner in the French Concession Special District Prison are formed into one group, and the 2 female prisoners in the British Concession are formed into one group. It is now decided that starting tomorrow (July 1st), one instructor will be assigned to each group to implement instruction for a period of three months, twice a week for one hour each time.

Instruction Methods Divided into Two Types: The instruction methods are divided into two types: 1. Group talks. 2. Individual talks. The instruction locations are divided into three places according to the location of each prison. Each place is divided into groups based on the number of prisoners and their level of education. An examination will be held at the end of each term. The instruction materials are compiled into a political training outline, first giving talks and then examining the prisoners' thinking. The instructors will also set subjects on an ad hoc basis. The instructors will report the progress of the instruction to the committee every week for review.

Inland River Shipping Association Explains Reasons for Requesting the Enactment of Regulations on the Shipping Industry 144

Previously, the newspaper reported that the Shipping Association's opinion on the shipping industry regulations was that the ocean and inland rivers should not be treated as one. Three opinions were stated, pointing out that the request was the private view of a part of the inland river small steamship industry. The reporter learned that the matter was handled by the Shanghai Municipal Inland River Shipping Association, which sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward it to the Executive Yuan for processing. A special visit was made to Mr. Han Yimin, the chairman of the association, who replied that the association's request to enact special regulations for the shipping industry was originally proposed for discussion at the current session of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Member Representatives' Meeting. However, because the meeting was adjourned before the discussion could take place, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Executive Yuan requesting that it be forwarded based on the review opinions, not just the private views of a part of the inland river small steamship industry. Moreover, it was confirmed by the committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce reviewing the proposal that it was a matter that should be handled. 1. Although the nature of the shipping industry and the electricity industry are different, they are both public utilities. Therefore, it is natural to apply the principle of supply and demand for public utilities and to have the competent authorities exercise rational supervision. The Regulations on the Supervision of Privately Operated Public Utilities already include shipping transportation. Why should there be any objection because the authorities in the past did not implement them? In addition to running a shipping business, I also run an electricity business and have been a member of the Supervisory Committee of the National Federation of Privately Operated Electric Power Industries and a member of the Standing Committee of the Zhejiang Branch of the Federation for many years. I know more about the past malpractices of the privately operated electric power industry, such as disputes over operating areas, the decay of power poles, the simplicity of power generation equipment, and the poor management of operations. These various ailments are just like the situation of the shipping industry today. However, since the Central Construction Commission established various special regulations and implemented supervision, standards for engineering and technology have been established, and rational protection, guidance, and suppression have been given to operations and management. Over the years, all the ailments have been reformed. It is difficult for the colleagues in the electric power industry to work hard on their own business. However, if there were no management regulations and the supervision of the competent authorities, I am afraid that this result could not be achieved. From this point of view, the association's request to enact shipping industry regulations is indeed a fundamental way to save China's shipping industry. 2. Although China's shipping industry has been restricted by unequal treaties and the loss of inland navigation rights, it is undeniable that the state-owned ships are old, and the operation is improper. At a time when commercial competition is becoming increasingly fierce, if there are no good laws to manage the shipping industry, not only will competition among colleagues be impossible to resolve, but also the attempt to recover navigation rights and develop the national shipping industry will be impossible to carry out. 3. In addition to the Maritime Law, the remaining shipping regulations, the various chapters on ship measurement and inspection, and the nationality certificate are all regulations solely governing ships, not laws for managing the shipping industry. This has resulted in shipping merchants having no protection in their business, and shipping route disputes are endless. In view of this, the association has requested the enactment of special regulations for the shipping industry as a fundamental solution. The association did not study it and hastily adjusted the existing regulations to be perfect. It has ignored the current ills of the shipping industry and failed to understand the purpose of the association's original proposal, which is regrettable. In short, China's shipping industry has a great and significant impact on national defense and political economy at this time of serious national crisis and national peril. It is the duty of the shipping administration authorities and shipping merchants to seek reasonable solutions. I hope that the government authorities and colleagues in various places will work together with a pragmatic approach to seek legitimate and reasonable ways to save the precarious shipping industry and complete the national defense. Fostering the country's interests and benefiting the people is not something that ignorant shipping merchants can gain or lose.

Ministry of Finance Salt Affairs Inspection Office Reorganized as a General Bureau by Order 145

To Be Implemented on July 1st with Expansion of Various Departments; Salt Affairs Division Also Renamed Salt Affairs Administration to Centralize Authority

The Ministry of Finance Salt Affairs Inspection Office has been ordered by the Ministry of Finance to be reorganized as a General Bureau starting from July 1st. All authority will be expanded compared to the present situation. All Salt Affairs Divisions will also be renamed Salt Affairs Administrations. Details of the situation are recorded below:

Reorganized as a General Bureau: In order to centralize the authority of salt affairs, unify inspections, and increase the efficiency of national tax revenue, the Ministry of Finance will expand the organization of salt affairs agencies, reorganizing the Salt Affairs Inspection Office currently stationed in Shanghai as a Salt Affairs General Bureau. The organizational charter has been passed by the Legislative Yuan. The Ministry of Finance has instructed the Inspection Office to implement the reorganization starting from July 1st, adopting a director-general system. The internal departments will also be expanded.

Establishment of Salt Administration: The highest agency for all matters concerning the management of salt affairs is the Salt Affairs Division of the Ministry of Finance. Previously, due to the expansion of the scope of salt affairs, the Ministry of Finance planned to improve the work by changing the Salt Affairs Division to the Salt Affairs Administration. The candidate for the director-general of the Administration is likely to be the current Director of the Division, Zhu Tingqi. Zhu will also concurrently serve as the Director-General of the Salt Affairs General Bureau.

Salt Mound Project: According to a Dagongshe reporter's investigation, the salt mounds built by the Ministry of Finance Salt Affairs Inspection Office in the salt areas on both sides of the Huainan and Huaibei areas are quite large in scale. The internal equipment for salt storage and salt production is arranged in the latest style. The salt mound projects on both sides have been completed, and it is expected that the output will increase year by year with this new equipment. Other salt production areas are also continuing to build in the same way.

Observatory Forecasts Hot Weather in the City Today; Local Thunderstorms Yesterday, But Still Sultry; Few Cases of Epidemic Disease; Sanitation Campaign Concluded 147

From the 27th to yesterday, the entire city was hit by a heat wave, with sultry heat that was suffocating. Although there was a temporary respite due to showers yesterday afternoon, the observatory reported that the weather will continue to be hot in the coming days. At this time of year, it will get hotter day by day. Yesterday's highest temperature was 94.6 degrees. This morning started out quite cool, but by 10:00 AM it gradually became hot. The standard thermometer at Xujiahui read 86 degrees, and by 11:30 AM, the thermometer had risen to 92.5 degrees. However, the outdoor temperature had already reached 97 degrees, which is a new record for this year.

Local Thunderstorms Offer Slight Relief

Between 11:00 AM and 12:00 PM today, the city experienced thunderstorms and torrential rain that poured down in an instant, driving away the scorching sun. However, the rain was only local at the time, extending only from Jing'an Temple to the Bund. West of Jing'an Temple, Xujiahui, Avenue Joffre, and the western district still did not see any rainfall, but there were dark clouds looming in the northeast. Later in the afternoon, the rain area expanded, and there was rainfall everywhere, intermittent and varying in intensity, resembling the plum rain season. The climate also cooled down slightly.

Epidemic Hospitals Crowded with Patients

Because citizens cannot endure the heat, they flock to places selling cold drinks, resulting in a threefold increase in business for ice cream parlors. Street vendors selling cold drinks are also crowded with laborers, but because the drinks are often unhygienically prepared, there is a risk of disease. Epidemic hospitals have sprung up in response. The Emergency Epidemic Hospital on Xizang Road is scheduled to open on the 1st of next month. The Hongkou Epidemic Hospital has already admitted patients. In addition, the Zhabei Public Hospital is also said to be opening at the same time as the Emergency Epidemic Hospital. According to reports from the city's health authorities, there are not many cases of epidemic disease reported in recent days.

Researching Prevention of Schistosomiasis

The Public Concession's Bureau of Health recently discovered schistosomes in the Luobiegen Road area of western Shanghai. These worms are hidden in unclean marshes. If people or animals swim in them, they can easily be infected, which poses a risk of spreading. A Dagongshe reporter learned yesterday morning that the Bureau of Health is now researching how to eliminate these dangerous worms. Many people have been affected by them, ranging from a pale complexion to the development of ascites. Therefore, they must be eliminated.

Sanitation Campaign Concludes Today

Since its launch, the city's 15th Sanitation Campaign has made every effort to promote summer sanitation, which has greatly benefited citizens. The campaign is scheduled to hold its closing ceremony at the Confucius Temple at 10:00 AM on the 30th to mark its conclusion.

River Robbery

The manufacturing machine was set up once when it was located on Met Hess Road. It had not been opened since it moved to Wuding Road. The second and third defendants were both orchid friends. Lin Ruitang also confessed that he was unemployed and helped Xiao. He also denied helping to make drugs. The police lawyer stated that Lin Ruitang also often went to Xiao's home. This time, the police station investigated Changping Road, and Lin guided them. A reporter from Datong News Agency investigated and recorded the situation as follows:

Committing Suicide by Jumping into the Sea The New Jiangtian Steamer set sail from Shanghai to Yong at 5 p.m. on the 27th. At that time, there was a middle-aged passenger in the first-class cabin of the ship. He also took the ship and planned to land in Zhenhai. At more than 11 o'clock that night, when the ship passed the waters of Wai Tongsha, the passenger suddenly left his berth and went elsewhere. At that time, the waiter in charge of the berth thought he was afraid of the noise and went to the deck to chat, but he never returned.

Discovery of Suicide Note The ship berthed in Zhenhai at about 4 a.m. the next morning. Although the waiter searched, he never found the passenger's trace. Then, he checked his berth and found a suicide note. The letter was written to his cousin Zhou Zipin, No. 2 Cunshuli, Muqiao Street, Nanshi, Shanghai. There were no other relics. The meaning of the book is to entrust his cousin to take care of the orphans.

Reason for Suicide Datong News Agency reporter visited Zhou Zipin at No. 2 Cunshuli, Senqiao Street, yesterday morning. According to Zhou, the deceased was extremely honest. Because I had an old relationship with the manager of the factory, I promoted him again and returned to his old position. Unexpectedly, someone slandered him to the manager and was dismissed. Now he is depressed.

Leaving Behind Orphans At the same time, the deceased's parents died and his wife died two years ago, leaving behind two daughters, both of whom are young. They are now in their hometown and are cared for by his old and dependent mother-in-law and grandmother. There is also a stepmother in Shanghai. The above relatives are all supported by the deceased. Therefore, the burden is heavy and the debts are heavy. The above reasons really started his suicide. However, the old parents and young daughters all depend on him for survival. He actually came up with this bad idea. It is really inconsiderate.

Huanghe Road Murder Case The Family of the Deceased Cries Out for Assistance 159

The case of Hua Bu shooting and killing Nantong personnel Shi Lin, which occurred in the Yihe Tea House on Huanghe Road, French Concession, this port, and the arrest of his younger brother Ji A'er by the French Police Station, recognizing him as having committed injury and attempted murder, and the prosecution in the Second Special District Local Court, which sentenced him to 20 days of detention the other day, and acquitted the rest of the defendants, have been reported in this newspaper many times. The Family of the Deceased Cries Out for Assistance from All Circles
