The bullet entered from the back and exited from the chest, and he ran to the door of the tailor shop at No. 8 Jialu Road and died on the spot. The patrol then arrested Mr. Li's husband, Ji A'er, on suspicion of harming Hua Detective, and prosecuted him in the Second Special District Local Court for attempted murder. He was sentenced to 20 days of detention the other day. The thought of the deceased's grievance has not been redressed, and her husband has been sentenced again. Such a grievance is truly shocking. Thinking that your association is a foundation for the citizens of this district and spares no effort to protect the citizens, I hereby present the situation of the incident in detail and cry out for assistance, asking you to uphold justice and give assistance to negotiate with the French authorities to bring the murderers to justice, so as to value human life and prevent the feelings from being 感 　.

The Fourth District Branch of the Second Special District Citizens' Association of this city received a petition from the family of the deceased requesting assistance. Since the matter concerns human life, it is specifically scheduled to convene an emergency meeting of all executive committee members at the association at No. 132 Bair Road at 5 p.m. on the 30th of this month (Tuesday) to discuss countermeasures. The corresponding letter is hereby sent to your committee member for your reference. Please be sure to attend on time and do not delay. It is also heard that the association has also sent a letter to the Nantong Fellow Villagers' Association and invited Lawyer Cai to attend to discuss countermeasures.

Two Shipping Accidents Reported 162

"Chun He" Grounded in Haizhou

The "Chun He" vessel, chartered by the Shanghai Mainland Industrial Company, with a deadweight of 1,765 tons, a length of 255 feet and 2 inches, a width of 35 feet and 2 inches, and a draft of 17 feet and 4 inches, was en route to Haizhou to load salt for the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. Yesterday, a telegram was received stating that when the "Chun He" finished loading in Haizhou and departed, the water level in Haizhou harbor was shallow, only about 12 feet at low tide. The "Chun He," fully loaded, had a draft of over 17 feet. Consequently, the ship ran aground at the harbor entrance, becoming stuck in the mud and unable to move at all. The shipowner tried various methods, including reversing the engine repeatedly, but failed to dislodge the vessel. Attempts to tow it also failed. Yesterday, the Shanghai company received this telegram, fearing prolonged grounding would damage the hull and cargo. They sent an urgent telegram to Haizhou, instructing the shipowner and the local salt depot authorities to hire large towing barges to quickly offload the salt from the "Chun He" to reduce its weight, and then arrange for a ship to tow the "Chun He" to safety.

"Ji Kang" Blown Ashore by Wind

The "Ji Kang" large iron barge belonging to Kang Zhen Ji in Shanghai, carrying a huge amount of goods, was transporting cargo from Lianyungang in the old kiln area of Haizhou. At 10 AM on the 27th of this month, a storm with heavy rain and turbulent waves, rarely seen before, occurred in Lianyungang. Many barges and civilian boats in the harbor were damaged or drifted away. The "Ji Kang" barge, located in the center of the harbor, was struck by a huge wave during the storm and blown directly onto a rocky beach. The bottom of the "Ji Kang" was completely broken on the rocks. The extent of the damage and loss is imaginable. The hull remains aground on the rocky beach, impossible to salvage. Yesterday, the ship's manager urgently telegraphed Shanghai, seeking instructions on rescue measures. The company is currently considering rescue plans.

Incident in the Second Special District Prison: Clash Between Chinese and Russian Inmates 163

In the Second Special District Prison on Route Massenet in the French Concession, at approximately 9 AM the day before yesterday, inmates Zhao Zhongheng, Tian Jinhai, Chen Dianxi, Lin Tingxi, and others, totaling fourteen, were taking a bath in the bathroom when they had a verbal argument with three Russian inmates over a minor issue. The argument escalated into a physical fight. Prison guards tried their best to stop them, but the inmates refused to comply and could not be controlled. The guards fired three warning shots into the air and telephoned the Lukiawan Police Station, requesting a large number of detectives to assist. The disturbance was eventually quelled. The detectives took the Chinese and Russian inmates involved in the incident, as well as the injured Russian inmates, back to the police station for questioning and sent them to the hospital for treatment. It is reported that the cause of the incident was that the Russian inmates had beaten a Chinese inmate the day before, causing injury. The remaining inmates then used this as an excuse to seek revenge. Another account suggests that the Russian inmates received better food and treatment than the Chinese inmates in prison, a privilege granted by the government, which led to resentment among the Chinese inmates. The French police are currently investigating the matter and will send the suspects to the Second Special Court for interrogation today.

"Great Evening Post" Reports: Car Hits Rickshaw Puller 164

Will the Police Prosecute?

According to the "Great Evening Post," a rickshaw puller was struck by a car on the Bund near the Garden Bridge at approximately 3:30 AM on Sunday morning, suffering serious injuries. Today (the 29th), the police are investigating the case. It is believed that the car involved bears license plate number 6767 from the Public Concession. It is reported that the owner is an official of the French Municipal Council, but he was not driving at the time of the accident. The Frenchman who was driving is believed to be an employee of the Shanghai Telephone Company. He was initially detained by the Old Zha Police Station for questioning and then handed over to the French police. This morning, various sources claimed that the Public Concession police would prosecute the driver, but others denied this, stating that the case is still under investigation and whether or not prosecution will occur is uncertain. The rickshaw puller's injuries were initially reported to be extremely serious, but it is now said that he may survive.

Boy Drowns While Bathing in Cold Water 165

A boy named Long Airang, a resident of Donggou Town in Pudong, only fourteen years old, went to Zhao Family River near his residence with neighboring children to cool off in the cold water, as the past two days have been exceptionally hot. However, Long was not a good swimmer and drowned, losing his life. When his family found out, they hired people to recover the body and reported the incident to the court for an examination.

Hotel Guest Attempts Suicide by Poisoning 166

A guest named Kong Yunwen, 29 years old, was staying in a room at the Runhua Hotel on Zhejiang Road. Yesterday morning at 7:30 AM, for reasons unknown, he secretly ingested poison and attempted suicide. He was discovered by the hotel staff, who rushed him to the hospital for treatment. However, the poisoning was severe, and he died at 8 AM. The body was sent to the coroner's office.

Tourist Commits Suicide by Poisoning in Old Juxing Hotel 167

A man calling himself Fang Anliang, 34 years old, from Anhui, checked into the Old Juxing Hotel on North Zhejiang Road in Zhabei the night before last. He took a small room and paid four small dollars for the room. Unexpectedly, at around 1 AM this morning, the guest suddenly began moaning in his room. The hotel accountant ordered the tea boy to open the door and found Fang pale and realized he had taken poison. He immediately reported it to the Tianbaoli Police Station of the Mongol Road Police Station, who dispatched police to send the guest to Pushan Hospital. Dr. Jia Shirong examined him and found that he had taken a large amount of tranquilizer pills and raw opium, so he died before treatment could be given. The incident has been reported to the court.

Yu Shanchen Seduces His Teacher's Wife 168

Caught Together in the Attic

Chen Qingyu, a local resident, lives at No. 24 Pingjiang Lane, Route Laveille in the French Concession. He has an elderly mother, and his wife, Shi Xiubao, is 34 years old and has three children. Yu Shanchen, a Ningbo native, is 23 years old. Introduced by a friend, he became Chen Qingyu's apprentice and regularly visited the Chen home. In February of this year, Chen's mother fell ill and was bedridden. Yu took advantage of the opportunity to have an affair with his teacher's wife, Shi Xiubao. Shi often made excuses to go out for secret meetings, and the affair had been going on for a long time. Chen Qingyu had heard rumors about this secret, but he lacked concrete evidence and had been secretly enduring it. The day before yesterday, Shi Xiubao again made an excuse to take her young son out. Chen found out and sent someone to secretly follow them. The follower saw Shi Xiubao carrying her son to No. 13 Dakang Lane on Baier Road. The follower saw a "For Rent" sign posted outside the house and pretended to be interested in renting the room. He learned that Shi Xiubao and Yu Shanchen were living together in the attic. He returned and reported this to Chen Qingyu. At 3 AM that night, Chen reported to the French police, who sent detectives to arrest Yu and Shi Xiubao and take them back to the police station. Yesterday, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Division of the Second Special Court. Judge Sun Pengxian presided over the hearing. 　The lawyer stated that the defendants were arrested for adultery. The investigation is not yet complete and requested a postponement. The plaintiff, Chen Qingyu, also submitted a statement of the case, requesting that it be handled according to the law. At that time, the defendants confessed to the crime. However, Shi Xiubao pointed out in court that her husband also had mistresses outside. The court verified the confession and rescheduled the hearing for July 7. The defendants were either released on bail or detained without bail.

A Scandal in the Buddhist Community 169

Monk Commits Violence Against Novice

The abbot Hong Kui of Longhua Temple was recently accused by a young novice, Yang Shoucheng, in a letter to the temple's Dharma protector, stating that Hong Kui had lured him to the meditation room and committed sodomy, causing injury to his anus. The Dharma protector, believing that the monk had violated the Buddhist precepts and broken the law, sent the novice Yang Shoucheng to the local court yesterday. After a preliminary hearing by Prosecutor Xie, the forensic doctor confirmed that it was not just one incident and that the anus was torn and fractured. The prosecutor immediately dispatched Wu Xisheng and Zhen Dong to Longhua Temple to arrest Monk Hong Kui and bring him to the court. He was immediately detained pending trial and legal defense.

News: Xiushan's Wife Disappears 170

Two People Involved are Arrested

Wen Xiushan (40 years old), a Fuding native residing at No. 31 Wuzhou Road, reported that his 21-year-old wife, Wu, went out to bathe at around 8 PM on the evening of the 9th of this month and suddenly disappeared. It was later discovered that Xiao Jinbao, a leather worker from the same village, had facilitated her affair with a Jiangbei native named Wang Debao. At that time, he hired a car to take Wu to a small inn on the Zhabei Han Bridge, where they stayed overnight. He then accompanied Wu to a hiding place in Ningbo. Wang Debao's mother, Ni, knew the information and reported it to the Jiaxing Road Police Station. The police first arrested Xiao Jinbao and then arrested Wang Ni at No. 21 Yangshupu Road. They were sent to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Fen presided over the hearing in the Third Criminal Court. Lawyer Zhang Shizhu of the Municipal Council stated that Wang Debao and Wen Wu's whereabouts are currently unknown, but the plaintiff, after mediation, will file a separate lawsuit in court. After questioning Wen Xiushan, he claimed that Zhang, the second landlord of Wang Ni, told him, "Your wife can be found. Don't pursue the matter." "I will definitely return Wu, and the result will be dropped." Wang Ni's attorney stated that Wu was not Wen's legal wife but a concubine. In May, due to disagreements between the two parties, a letter was sent through Lawyer Ma to sever their relationship as husband and concubine. It was questioned that after his wife died, he married Wu Mao as his successor, not as a concubine. They were married last June, and her parents now live at No. 77 Shenjiatan, Yangshupu, and can testify in court next time. Judge Xiao questioned the two defendants and their confessions remained the same. He ordered them to be detained and the case continued to be verified.

Central Bank Inspection Report 172

The 289th Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of Central Bank Exchange Certificates states: In accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, the Council is responsible for inspecting the number of exchange certificates issued by the Bank and the reserve fund. The 289th inspection was held in the Issuance Bureau of the Bank on June 27, 1936. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of exchange certificates issued is 29,925,315.25 silver dollars, including 26,802,318 silver dollar certificates and 3,122,994.45 auxiliary currency certificates. The total amount of exchange certificate reserve fund is 29,915,315.15 silver dollars, including 20,188,182.5 silver dollars in cash reserve. The cash reserve is deposited in the Bank's issuing branch and various branches, totaling 11,339,189.77.1 yuan, and deposited in other banks, totaling 8,848,892.72.9 yuan. The guaranteed reserve is converted into 9,737,130 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold exchange certificates issued is 400,963.07 yuan. The total amount of customs gold exchange certificate reserve fund is 400,963.07 yuan. The reserve fund includes 7,926.290 ounces of pure gold, valued at 51.68, totaling 400,963.07 yuan. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve should be at least 60%, and the remainder should be guaranteed with legal guarantees. The inspection results show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guaranteed reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the law. This report is hereby issued. June 29, 1936, Chairman of the Supervisory Board of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun, Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiyu.

The 30th Anniversary of the Opening of Huacheng Insurance Company 173

Expanding Business, Moving to a New Building

Huacheng Insurance Company was founded in the 32nd year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty. The founders, such as Zeng Shaoqing, Zhu Baosan, Yu Pinghan, Shen Manyun, Li Yunshu, Li Pingqi, Wang Yiting, Gu Xinyi, Mu Shuzai, and others, were all prominent figures in Shanghai at the time. They were aware of the development of foreign-owned insurance companies, the outflow of profits, and the increasing leakage of funds. They also believed that insurance was essential to the lives and property of the people and that Chinese people were often at a disadvantage due to a lack of understanding of insurance regulations. Therefore, they resolutely established the Huacheng Insurance Company, a completely Chinese-owned company, to protect profits and safeguard the property of their fellow countrymen, and to contribute to the development of Nanshi. They specially set up a shoe company outside the Malu Bridge. All sectors of Shanghai learned about the Chinese-owned insurance company and that its founders were the most reputable figures in the area. People flocked to take out insurance policies, and the business flourished. The first manager of the company was Mr. Huang Youlin, followed by Li Pingqing, Wen Nuzai, and Gu Xinyi, all of whom prioritized the well-being of the people. They were particularly prompt in settling claims and never made things difficult for customers. Huaxing, Huacheng, and Huaan Insurance Companies rose one after another, deeply gaining social trust and laying a solid foundation for the Chinese insurance industry. Subsequently, more Chinese insurance companies were established, and there are now more than twenty, enough to compete with foreign companies. Foreign-owned companies, seeing the rise of Chinese companies and their growing influence, engaged in price reductions and commission increases, leading to fierce competition. The company, observing the trend, had to change its approach and work hard. In May of this year, it convened a shareholders' meeting, re-elected directors and supervisors, and elected Zhang Zhuping as chairman of the board, Wang Yiting and Gu Xinyi as directors. Wan, Huang Xingjie, Sheng Zeheng, Dong Haoguang, Yu Ziqi, and Li Zhishi as directors, and Guo Fuyun and Liu Hengfu as supervisors. To commemorate the 30th anniversary of the company's founding and to encourage future development, it was decided to expand the scope of business, including fire insurance, water insurance, automobile insurance, war risk insurance, and accident insurance. Branch offices and agencies were gradually established in various provinces and cities to attract business. The original headquarters was too small, so the company moved to 467 Jiangxi Road, and a reception was held on July 1 for all sectors to tour the premises. The general manager of the company is Qin Ziqi, a veteran in the insurance industry, the manager is Li Dingshi, and the deputy managers are Ye Junfa, Wang Yihe, Xie Shunzhi, and Yao Mingru. It is expected that the company will continue to serve the community sincerely with its 30 years of reputation and experience, and will surely shine in the Chinese insurance industry.

Xinxin Company Changes Business Hours. The weather has been hot lately, and going out at noon is quite difficult. The Xinxin Company on Nanjing Road has decided to slightly change its business hours from July 1st to adapt to the environment. Weather Report 184

The Zikawei Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the area around Shandong, the middle reaches of the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers, would experience northwest to northeast winds. The middle reaches of the Yangtze River and the Hankou area, as well as the lower reaches of the Yangtze River and this area, would be cloudy and hot, with thunderstorms and uncertain wind directions. The East China Sea and Taiwan would transition from cloudy to foggy, with possible showers and southeast to northeast winds. Also, the highest temperature in the port within the 24 hours before 2:00 PM yesterday was 94.3 degrees, and the lowest was 76.8 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 83.8 degrees, and the lowest was 76.1 degrees.

China Youth Physical Education Department Organizes Water Polo Training Class 186

The China Youth Physical Education Department is sparing no effort in promoting swimming. This swimming season, in addition to continuing to run summer swimming classes for students, it is also organizing a water polo training class, scheduled to start on the 6th of next month. In addition, the Cooperative Tennis Club, organized by members of the association, will also hold a get-together. Details are as follows:

Water Polo Training Water polo is quite popular in Hong Kong and Guangdong. In Shanghai, only the Malta team had such an organization in the past. Even those who practice it have immature skills. Skilled water polo players must possess both wrestling and sprinting abilities. It is the most complete water sport in terms of strength, so learning water polo is more difficult than other ball sports and cannot be achieved overnight. This season, the China Youth Association has decided to open a water polo training class to cultivate talent in this area. The quota is twenty people, and many have already signed up. The training time will be arranged after the enrollment quota is met.

Lifesaving Training Lifesaving is a specialized skill, so those who are proficient in swimming may not be able to perform lifesaving and rescue. Necessary methods must be used. The association is establishing a lifesaving class this season, with a quota of twenty people. However, applicants must pass an exam and meet the following qualifications: (A) Able to swim freestyle, breaststroke, sidestroke, and backstroke (without using hands) for 40 yards continuously; (B) Able to jump into the water from a springboard; (C) Able to dive from a water surface eight feet deep and retrieve an eight-pound object. The association will also award medals to those who pass the exam upon completion of the course to encourage them.

Beginner Swimming Class This season's beginner swimming class has received a very enthusiastic response. Training is scheduled to start on the 6th of next month, every Tuesday, Thursday, and Saturday from 8:00 PM to 9:00 PM at the association's swimming pool on Sichuan Road. This class is specifically designed for beginners and uses simple and quick methods to teach various swimming techniques. Each class has a quota of twenty-five people. A second class will be added when the quota is met.

Tennis Social Gathering The Cooperative Tennis Club, organized by members of the association, has about forty members this year. However, due to work commitments, the players are divided into morning and evening classes, and their schedules differ, making it difficult for team members to meet. To promote connections, the association has scheduled a social gathering game at the Luzon Road court next month on the 4th (Saturday) afternoon. A dinner is also planned at the Chengdu Restaurant that evening.

Reuters Dispatch from Milwaukee, USA, 28th: Marius of Denver, Colorado, set a new world record in the decathlon at the Olympic trials today, with a total score of 7880 points. The old record was 7824.5 points, set by the German Olympic athlete Sievert in 1934.

Wuhan City Public Boat Race 189

Thirty-Two Dragon Boats, 200,000 Spectators

Central News Agency Dispatch from Hankou, 28th: The first Wuhan City public boat race was held at Aijiazui Zongguan in Xianghe on the 28th, with a total distance of 5200 meters. Thirty-two dragon boats participated, with the most rowers being over 160 and the least being 18. The boats ranged in length from nine to two zhang. The race was divided into five groups. The number of spectators on both sides reached 200,000, an unprecedented event in recent decades. Before the race, Yang Yongtai, Chen Panling, and Wu Guozhen addressed the athletes, encouraging them to commemorate their ancestors, promote national sports, strictly observe the order of things, and work together. The race ended at 3:00 PM, with five boats including the Chenyuan Gang winning first place with a time of 28 minutes and 56 seconds. However, in the final performance group, one boat, the Kouwai Wujia, was damaged by the Guansheng Temple boat. Fortunately, all the rowers who fell into the water were rescued. Only Jiang Xucai suffered minor injuries.

University of Heidelberg, Germany, Confers Honorary Doctorate on Wang Jingwei 197

(Central News Agency Dispatch from Berlin, 29th) The University of Heidelberg, Germany, the second most famous university in the world, will confer an honorary doctorate in political economy on Wang Jingwei tomorrow at its 550th-anniversary celebration and invite Wang to give a speech at the university. Wang is very grateful but regrets that he cannot attend in person due to illness. He has asked the Chinese Embassy in Germany to accept the degree on his behalf.

General Situation of National Higher Education in the 22nd Year 198

The Ministry of Education recently compiled statistics on the general situation of national colleges and universities (including universities, independent colleges, and vocational schools) in the 22nd year. The main points are summarized below:

Number of Schools and Their Distribution

There are 108 colleges and universities this year, including 29 vocational schools, 39 independent colleges, and 40 universities. In terms of nature, there are 22 national schools (13 universities, 5 colleges, and 4 vocational schools), 6 ministry-run schools (vocational schools), 29 provincial schools (7 universities, 12 colleges, and 10 vocational schools), and 51 private schools (20 universities, 22 colleges, and 9 vocational schools). Their distribution can be divided into four major centers: the north, with Tianjin and Beijing totaling 23 schools; the south, with Guangzhou totaling 8 schools; the east, with Nanjing and Shanghai totaling 29 schools; and the central region, with Sichuan, Hubei, Henan, and Hunan totaling 15 schools. The detailed distribution is as follows: Shanghai 24, Beijing 16, Hebei 9, Guangdong 8, Hubei 6, Jiangsu 6, Beijing 5, Shanxi 5, Zhejiang 4, Fujian 4, Sichuan 4, Henan, Shandong, and Jiangxi each 3, Hunan 2, Guangxi, Anhui, Yunnan, Gansu, Shaanxi, and Xinjiang each 1.

Sources and Distribution of Funds The total annual income of national colleges and universities is over 34.54 million yuan. The sources are over 20.2 million yuan from national and provincial treasuries (over 14.73 million yuan from the national treasury and over 5.46 million yuan from the provincial treasury), over 3.98 million yuan from student fees (over 2.6 million yuan in tuition, over 1.34 million yuan in miscellaneous fees, over 100,800 yuan in experimental fees, over 139,000 yuan in lecture note fees, over 115,000 yuan in library fees, and over 977,000 yuan in other fees), over 820,000 yuan in rent and interest, and over 6.73 million yuan in donations. The total annual expenditure is over 33.57 million yuan. The distribution is over 19.25 million yuan in salaries (over 11.9 million yuan in teacher salaries, over 4.03 million yuan in staff salaries, and over 1.24 million yuan in wages), over 6.37 million yuan in equipment expenses, over 3.8 million yuan in office expenses, over 2.4 million yuan in special expenses, and over 1.64 million yuan in expenses for affiliated institutions.

School Organization National colleges and universities are divided into 198 colleges, 668 departments, 59 subjects, and 97 groups. Universities and independent colleges are organized into colleges, with departments under the colleges. Their affiliated vocational schools are organized in the same way as vocational schools, divided into several subjects, with groups under the subjects. The nature of colleges, departments, subjects, and groups can be divided into two categories: liberal arts (literature and art, law and politics, education, commerce) and sciences (science, agriculture, engineering, medicine).

General Equipment A. School land can be divided into construction land, sports fields, farms, forests, gardens, etc. The largest construction land in the country is over 1766 mu (National Shandong University), and the smallest is only 2 mu (National Shanghai Medical College). The largest sports field is 822 mu (Shandong University), and the smallest is 6 fen (Provincial Hunan University). The largest farm is 9840 mu (National Sun Yat-sen University), and the smallest is 1 mu and 2 fen (Private Fudan University). The largest garden is 1093 mu (Shandong University), and the smallest is 1 fen (Hunan University). The largest forest is 36667 mu (Private Nantong College), and the smallest is 2 mu and 6 fen (Hunan University). The largest total school area is 37019 mu and 6 fen (Private Nantong College), and the smallest is only 2 mu (National Shanghai Medical College). The most valuable school land is worth over 1.84 million yuan (Private Qilu University), and the least is worth about 4,000 yuan (Provincial Henan Water Conservancy Engineering Vocational School). B. The school with the most rooms has over 3,000 rooms (Beijing University), and the school with the fewest rooms has only over 10 rooms (Shanghai Veterinary Vocational School). The largest total school capacity can accommodate over 10,500 people (Sichuan University), and the smallest can accommodate only over 80 people (Private Shanghai Women's Medical College). The school with the most classrooms has over 300 classrooms (Beijing University), and the school with the fewest classrooms has only 12 classrooms. The largest total classroom capacity can accommodate over 3,200 people (Peking University), and the smallest can accommodate only over 40 people (Private Wuchang Wenhua Library Science Vocational School). The largest auditorium capacity can accommodate over 4,000 people (Sichuan University), and the smallest can accommodate only over 100 people (National Music Vocational School). The largest library capacity can accommodate 600 people (Wuhan University), and the smallest can accommodate over 10 people. The largest total laboratory capacity can accommodate over 2,000 people (Tsinghua University), and the smallest can accommodate over 10 people. C. The value of teaching and school equipment is over 18.9 million yuan (over 14.91 million yuan for teaching equipment and over 4.02 million yuan for school equipment). D. Libraries hold a total of 4.49 million books, an increase of over 540,000 books compared to the previous year. According to Dewey's classification, there are over 1.023 million books in the general category, over 690,000 books in literature, over 501,000 books in social sciences, over 480,000 books in history and geography, over 215,000 books in natural sciences, over 200,800 books in applied sciences, over 206,000 books in philosophy, over 100,300 books in fine arts, over 90,000 books in language, and over 79,000 books in religion. E. The value of new equipment added this year is over 6.37 million yuan.

Faculty and Staff There are a total of over 7,200 faculty and staff (including over 1,080 part-time staff) and over 5,100 staff (including over 1,080 part-time teachers). Therefore, the actual total number of faculty and staff is over 11,300 (faculty and staff who hold both positions are counted as one person). Among the faculty, there are 6,720 men and 489 women. Among the staff, there are 4,828 men and 362 women. Among the faculty, there are 3,130 professors and associate professors, 2,462 lecturers, 1,060 teaching assistants, and 513 unranked staff. Among the staff, there are 113 presidents (including 2 vice-presidents), 88 deans of academic affairs, 143 secretaries, 133 college deans, 633 department heads, 74 business managers, 508 section chiefs, 1,075 section members, 1,013 clerks, 739 scribes, and 671 others.

Enrolled Students There are a total of over 42,090 students, including over 37,600 students in universities and independent colleges and over 5,300 students in affiliated vocational schools and vocational schools. Over 28,700 students are in liberal arts subjects, and over 14,100 students are in science subjects. The oldest student is over 30 years old, and the youngest student is under 17 years old. There are over 7,100 students who are 23 years old, making 23 the most common age for college students in the country. The national average age is 23.43 years old.

Graduates A total of 8,665 people graduated, including 6,750 from universities and 1,915 from vocational schools. Of these, 29.57% are in science subjects and 70.43% are in liberal arts subjects.

Municipal Elementary and Secondary Schools in the City to Collect Health Fees Starting Next Year Middle School Students 2 Jiao, Elementary School Students 1 Jiao to be Collected by the Schools at the Beginning of Each Semester 201

In order to promote health education, the Municipal Health Education Committee has obtained approval from the Bureau of Education to collect health fees from private elementary and secondary schools in the city starting from the 25th year. The method is that middle school students will pay 2 jiao of legal tender per person per semester, and elementary school students will pay 1 jiao of legal tender per person per semester. The fees will be temporarily collected from public and private schools in the city and will be collected by the schools at the beginning of each semester. All elementary and secondary school students in the city who pay the health fee will be entitled to all the rights of the committee to implement school health.

National Academic Employment Counseling Center: Unemployment Statistics for Students 202

Registered: 2,025 people; Successfully Placed: 195 people

The National Academic Employment Counseling Center, since its establishment in October 1934, has been conducting a new survey of unemployed students with specialized education or higher and its job placement services in various regions up to April of this year, a brief account of which has been published in this newspaper. Herewith is a detailed statistical record published by the Center:

Returned Students: The statistics for returned students were obtained through surveys, with 2,770 questionnaires received. 161 in Literature, 313 in Science, 511 in Law, 153 in Education, 233 in Agriculture, 872 in Engineering, 158 in Commerce, 277 in Medicine, 18 in Navy, 53 in Army, 32 in Aviation, 11 Unknown. Job Placement: The Center's method of job placement for the unemployed is as follows: Organizations or individuals in need of talent request assistance from the Center. The Center, upon learning of an opportunity for talent at a certain place, automatically introduces suitable registered individuals. In total, 253 requests were received by the Center. Geographically, requests came from as far inland as Ningxia in China and as far abroad as Korea, Burma, and Southeast Asia. There was a need for a total of 383 talents. 195 people were successfully placed, and a total of 719 people were recommended. Regarding salary, the lowest monthly salary was 10 yuan, and the highest was 480 yuan. Based on the 195 successful placements, the total monthly salary was 17,355 yuan.

Yu Zhao-ming to Study Vocational Education in the United States 207

Mr. Yu Zhao-ming, styled Jianqing, is a Bachelor of Arts from the University of Nanking, the Director of Academic Affairs and Director of Life Guidance at the First Municipal Middle School of Nanking, a middle school teacher at the Nanjing YMCA, and the Chief Officer of the Nanking Office of the China Vocational Education Society. He has served diligently for nine years and has authored books such as "Vocational Guidance in Various Countries," "Guidance for Secondary and Primary School Students on Further Education and Employment," and "Vocational Guidance for Primary Schools," all published by the Commercial Press. This time, in order to pursue further studies and specialize in vocational education and vocational guidance, he has resigned from various positions and is going to the United States to study at the University of California, majoring in education. Mayor Ma of Nanking, recognizing his specialization in vocational education and appreciating Mr. Yu's outstanding achievements during his tenure in the city of Nanking, has specifically approved him to study education in the United States and has granted him a stipend to encourage him. It is heard that Mr. Yu recently came to Shanghai to complete出国手续. The China Vocational Education Society Jiang Wen-yu, Yang Wei, Wang He-qing, Pan Yang-yao, Shi Yang-yong, Yang Chong-gao, and others, hosted a farewell banquet and discussed all matters. It has been decided that he will depart on the President Jackson on the 21st of next month.

Graduation Ceremonies 209

Municipal Council Girls' School

The Shanghai Municipal Council Girls' School held its 3rd graduation ceremony on the 27th on campus. Chairman Seidler of the Municipal Council's Education Department and Mrs. Niu Hui-sheng delivered speeches, Chen He-qin presented diplomas, and Xi Yu-shu awarded prizes. Many parents and guests attended. Graduates of the school are required to pass joint examinations by the Municipal Council and the Municipal Education Bureau, so the students' academic level is particularly high. Most graduates are preparing for further education, with a few entering the workforce.

McTyeire School

McTyeire School held its 30th graduation ceremony at 10:00 AM on the 29th. Principal Yang first reported that the number of graduates this year was 37 from senior high, 49 from junior high, and 1 from the piano department. She also mentioned a noteworthy coincidence: the mothers of two sisters in the senior high department were both graduates of the same class in 1907, namely Mrs. He Qing-tai and Mrs. Li Qing-mao, and now their daughters are also graduating from the same class at the school. The school's operations, curriculum, discipline, and management have all undergone significant improvements. This was followed by a speech by Huang Ren-zhi. After the speech, the principal presented diplomas, and the school song was sung. The ceremony then concluded.

Zhen Xing Girls' Middle School

Since Shen Junru became the principal of Zhen Xing Girls' Middle School on Avenue Foch, he has worked hard to reorganize it. Yesterday, the high school and junior high school graduation ceremony was held at 9:00 AM. Principal Shen delivered a speech, followed by speeches from guests and representatives of all the faculty and staff. Finally, the graduating class representative gave a response. The school is scheduled to hold the first entrance examination for new students on July 13th and 14th.

Nie Zhongcheng Public School

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Nie Zhongcheng Chinese Public School held its graduation ceremony yesterday morning at 10:00 AM. In addition to more than one hundred parents of students, Kang of the Municipal Council Education Department, Chen Heqin, Director of Chinese Education, Shen Yi, Director of Shanghai Municipal Works Bureau, and Thomson were also present. After the ceremony, Principal Ke Xiao reported on school affairs, and students gave performances. Finally, Thomson awarded prizes and the meeting adjourned.

Soochow Zhenhua Girls' School

The Soochow Zhenhua Girls' School held its closing ceremony on the morning of the 27th. The ceremony was simple but solemn. Because the high school joint examinations had not yet been announced, only a completion ceremony was held, while graduation ceremonies were held for the junior high school and elementary school. The high school graduating class was the 15th, with a total of 41 students. The junior high school graduating class was the 12th, with a total of 82 students. Current Situation of Xin Huan Vocational School

The Xin Huan Vocational School, located at the intersection of Chongqing Road and Weihaiwei Road in this city, was founded by Mr. Zhang Xinbo and Mr. Zhang Zhonghuan who sacrificed their homes to establish it. In the past three years, its achievements have been remarkable, and the progress of school affairs has been particularly astonishing. The school has convenient transportation, a serene environment, magnificent buildings, spacious grounds, and has been fully equipped with books, instruments, specimens, as well as Chinese and English typing rooms, commodity display rooms, statistical practice rooms, and bank and shop practice workshops. The teachers are mostly well-known scholars in China, who teach diligently. Teaching emphasizes practice, exercises, discussions, and extracurricular research. Training implements the integration of teaching and training, and the class teacher system, emphasizing spiritual training, adopting personality edification, and strictly enforcing gatekeeping, limiting expenses, and emphasizing cleanliness, labor discipline, and courtesy. Physical education also emphasizes universality, implementing military management, high school emphasizes military training, and junior high school emphasizes Boy Scouts. Currently, there are senior high and junior high school commerce courses and applied chemistry courses, with approximately 500 students. The graduates have excellent career prospects. It is heard that the school has been registered with the Municipal Education Bureau, and it plans to expand the school buildings and add classes after the summer. Enrollment is scheduled for July 9th and 10th, and there has been quite a rush to request prospectuses and register.

The percentage of graduates who are admitted to provincial-level secondary schools is extremely high each year. The school is currently planning to expand the number of places.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 235

—(Rong Yu)

"Reading sound, weaving sound, child crying sound." In the old days, having these three sounds was considered an auspicious omen for the family. Modern families are different now, and they constantly have "radio broadcast sounds, mahjong clicking sounds, and the sound of wives and concubines scolding." Are these three sounds good or bad? I still need to ask the readers to comment.

People in the past said, "If you can bite into the vegetable root, then everything can be done." This was to encourage people to "endure the bitterness of the bitter, and then become a person above people." Nowadays, unless disaster victims have nothing to eat, they are willing to bite into vegetable roots. Otherwise, once they get a little success, they want to be rich and honored, and they are not willing to put effort into these little things!

Buying tickets at the theater, getting on and off transportation, we Chinese people habitually "do not give way to righteousness, but rush to be first." If we put this courage on the battlefield, foreigners would definitely retreat three times.

Robbers are indeed hateful, but he doesn't rob others, but he robs you, and you also have a place to attract misfortune. If you don't know how to improve yourself, but complain that people are barbaric and unreasonable, I ask if this grievance can move God, and know how to win? If you know that it can't, it's better not to complain, but to bury your head in hard work.

Sunlight 236

— Wei Jing

The sun unconditionally casts its light, and mankind on Earth unconditionally absorbs sunlight. This seems like the fairest thing in the world. But while this statement is perfectly reasonable in the countryside, in this, the only metropolis in the East, a question mark, shaped like an ear, should be added to it.

In the countryside, on vast farms, with only three thatched cottages standing alone, as long as the weather is clear, regardless of heat or cold, from the moment the sun rises from the horizon until it sets again, the sunlight bathes every part of the surroundings. The people in the thatched cottages can fully enjoy the immeasurable heat and the germ-killing power, as scientists call it, within the sunlight.

But in our metropolis, sunlight is considered a highly precious commodity. For houses of the same size, the front building facing south is always twice as expensive as the rear building facing north, because the southern one can enjoy or at least see sunlight throughout the year, while the northern one has no chance to be in contact with sunlight at all. Similarly, on a three-story building, one with a skylight on the roof is surely eight dimes or one dollar more expensive per month than one without, because sunlight shines through the skylight.

According to foreigners' investigations, in lane houses, there are cases where seven or eight families live behind a single stone-framed gate, and some of them never receive any sunlight throughout the year. This is very inappropriate in terms of hygiene. These words are correct from a hygienic standpoint, but how can those foreigners living in Western-style houses with gardens understand that in this city, sunlight is a luxury that one has to pay a high price for, and that not everyone has the right to enjoy it? Therefore, in general lane houses, the competition for a place on the drying platform often becomes the focal point of conflict among cohabitants, because the supply of sunlight is too scarce, and it is too precious.

I once had a foolish idea: to put the inexpensive sunlight from the countryside into bottles, or boxes, or some other kind of container, and transport it to the city to sell. But on second thought, this is somewhat pointless, because people who can't afford to live in a house with sunlight probably don't have spare money to buy sunlight to enjoy either.

Bean Curd Labor 237

— Fan Xianwei

Grinding bean curd is one of the three most arduous jobs under heaven; everyone acknowledges that. In fact, among the three, blacksmithing and rowing boats are somewhat better. They work during the day and can sleep peacefully in bed at night, dreaming good dreams. One night of rest restores their spirit and strength. Only the bean curd workers truly suffer! Working during the day is not the main issue; it's that they must strain themselves in the dark midnight, "glug, glug," working frantically. In summer nights, mosquitoes swarm all over their bodies, foul odors fill their nostrils, sweating profusely, swatting mosquitoes and scratching itches. Winter nights are even worse, needless to say. They are jolted out of a good sleep, climb out of a warm bed, teeth chattering, a lamp flickering dimly, the bellows "crack-crack," the millstone "glug-glug," together forming a twisted labor song.

It's said: Although the trade is lowly, the profits are substantial. In the past, there were the "wine vat," "dye vat," and "bean curd vat," known as "hidden door" businesses. Now other businesses are experiencing economic downturns, but bean curd shops are still doing well, indicating that their profits are indeed high! Overseas Chinese in Paris, known as the "Three Heroes of Bean Curd," have actually accumulated vast fortunes through this smelly business. Who would have thought that this small, lowly trade could become famous abroad!

Others say: Bean curd shop owners certainly have it good, but pity those bean curd workers. Their work is heavy, and their pay is low. It truly only prevents starvation. If you don't believe me, look at their bodies; aren't they all broken and worn out, like living beggars!

Replacing the Nest, Mating Phoenixes 239

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Three: The Rain and Slanting Wind Leave Traces; In the Still Night, a Letter of Severance is Written.

Precisely because of this, he reached out his snow-white hand to hold back the rain curtain and stretched his head outside. The slanting wind blew raindrops onto his face, but he didn't seem to mind, his eyes fixed forward. Guoshi saw him and made a slight nod of acknowledgement. He was not so wooden and unmoved; he smiled faintly at Guoshi. The rickshaw puller thought the female student sitting in his cart must be eager to get home, so he pulled the cart quickly. Therefore, the time the two faced each other was extremely short. At that moment, Guoshi didn't even have time to smile a second time, let alone speak. It rained again for three days, and he always sat in the cart. On the fourth day, the weather was very sunny. Thinking that he would be walking today, he mustered up one hundred and twenty percent of his courage. He felt that he had been too timid in the past. As a man, if he didn't even dare to ask a friend's name, he might as well not bother with social interactions. Fortunately, he had already figured out how to start a conversation. Now he just needed to practice his delivery. Upon seeing him, he must not panic, and naturally not be shy. He would stand firm, give a deep nod, and then say, "Miss, we see each other every day, we're quite familiar. May I ask for your esteemed surname?" She would certainly stop, smile, and say, "You are too kind." Then, she would generously give her name. This time, he could only take the conversation this far. Anything more would have to wait for next time. Having made up his mind, as he walked into the lane where they usually met that morning, his heart began to race. By the time the person walked in front of him, his face was flushed. Not only could he not speak, he even forgot the slight nod he usually gave. He simply lowered his head and walked past. By the time the person had walked far away, he regretted it, but it was too late to make amends. Because he had acted somewhat flustered that time, he dared not attempt it that afternoon. The next day, he rallied his courage again. As he left home, his feet felt particularly firm on the ground, and each step was louder, as if he were demonstrating his resolve. When he reached the lane, he peeked at the approaching young lady from afar. Her attire was neat, but her face was cast downward, as if she was angry. "Is she angry at me?" "Slow down, slow down, I can't take the risk today. There's plenty of time, I'll wait for an opportunity." So, in this hesitation, another four or five days passed. However, things were a bit different during these four or five days. Sometimes he would see her, sometimes not. (41)

Special Feature

On the Shanghai-Suzhou Highway 240

— Yafei

I had long wanted to make a pilgrimage to several highways, but due to lack of opportunity, I finally shelved this concern, and gradually forgot it.

The day before yesterday, in order to investigate the living conditions in the countryside, I revived that forgotten impulse. In a hazy, moonlit morning, in a new model silver car, I climbed onto that long, winding highway.

We departed from Sichuan Road, passing through a corner of the metropolis, which was still asleep. Later, we went out from Zhabei, passed the Sun Temple. The horn roared like a beast, the car flew like lightning, and we quickly left behind some shacks and some working people. What appeared before us was a vast and boundless plain.

The sky gradually brightened. Some places were sprinkled with a layer of lovely golden sunlight. A morning breeze, tinged with the scent of the season, poked its head in through the car window, lightly kissing my face. My heart was filled with excitement and joy!

After the car passed Zhenru, it was like a small, unmoored boat in the sea of nature, speeding along the highway. The car body shook like a small boat in the waves. The scents of wheat and flowers, carried by the lonely morning breeze, reminded me that it was the season for reaping wheat and sowing seeds.

Advancing towards the depths of the plain, many fields and paths flashed past my eyes clearly and vaguely. Near the railway, I could see the third and fourth-class passenger trains departing from Shanghai, rushing forward like terrible beasts. The rumbling sound shook the earth, and sharp cries sliced through the solidified sky, causing the still air to tremble.

Puffs of black smoke, like blackened cotton wads, were spewed out from the "dragon head," abandoned in the sky, drifting in the suburbs—

In the fields, there were already scattered farmers working: men and women, some standing ploughing the soil, some bending over reaping wheat and pulling beans, and some already transplanting rice in the shallow paddy fields.

Villages, fields, bridges... all slipped past my eyes. Two hours later, that gray, ancient city wall lay before me like a dead snake. Soon, I ordered the car to stop at Xinlumen. I looked at my watch. It was exactly seven o'clock, and the Shanghai Daily Public Association's newspaper delivery car had already arrived in Suzhou.

Seaside Sketch 241

— Feng Moni

"Going to the sea?!"

Bare-legged, carrying fishing gear, a group went towards the Yellow Sea. They are fishermen who catch cicada larvae and depend entirely on the Yellow Sea for their livelihood. Because they don't have money to build seagoing boats, they catch cicada larvae on the beach to sell in the city.

They understand the tides. After the tide recedes, the cicada larvae are all on the beach, making them easy to catch. Each person squats down, toes sinking into the mud, a smile on their face, catching cicada larvae and throwing them into their fishing baskets, singing a tune without rhythm. Many footprints float on the beach.

"Rumble! Rumble!"

Two black oxen, pulling a cart, go into the sea. A fisherman sits on the back of the ox, and the cart is piled high with fishing nets. This is a Shanghai boat, preparing to fish when the tide comes tomorrow.

The desolate beach is dotted with a few thatched huts. The soil turns a layer of snow-white salt after being exposed to the sunlight. The white, vast water seems to connect to the sky. Only a few sea boats are parked in the sea, and some are stranded on the beach. One can still see ox carts moving in the water. How fierce the sea breeze is! Standing there is somewhat swaying, and the heads of the fishermen on the beach are wriggling. "Going to the market!"

The fishing baskets are filled with cicada larvae. They stand up and run, there are still fifteen li to Changsha. Several legs quickly pass by, still estimating the value of the cicada larvae in the fishing baskets, fifty coppers (note), eighty coppers, but not more than one hundred coppers.

Many fishermen, exposed to the sunlight, are burning all over, sweat dripping from their foreheads, bare-shouldered, carrying fishing baskets and running, running along the ox cart tracks, gradually disappearing in a corner of the beach. (Note) Copper coins

Wandering in the Arts

Reading Paintings in Cun Tian Ge 242

— Lu Yinquan

Mr. Hai Su is about to exhibit several hundred of his masterpieces to the nation in Shanghai. Through the introduction of Shao Hou, I was fortunate to get a preview in Cun Tian Ge.

I am a layman when it comes to Western painting, and although the Pavilion is filled with a dazzling array of paintings, I initially dared not utter a word. But after seeing his "Yellow Mountain" and "Withered Lotus" works, I was struck by how he used passionate oil paints to express the elegant and unrestrained spirit of traditional Chinese painting. His creative power and freedom are compelling.

The Pavilion owner's earlier traditional Chinese paintings were mostly bold and vigorous in brush and ink, uninhibited and unrestrained. Their majestic spirit and unrestrained emotions leapt off the paper, daring one to look up. The new works have a slightly different style, moving from majesty to inner refinement, from unrestrained to rigorous and precise. Because he has cultivated deeply and accumulated richly, he can, like one who tames the sea, clearly distinguish and arrange; like one who washes snow and chews ice, return to purity and integrity; and like one whose work is effortless, return to nature.

The Pavilion owner discussed Chinese painting with me, saying: "Buddhism came to the East and, influenced by it, art greatly advanced. However, throughout the Six Dynasties, Sui, and Tang dynasties, it was subordinate to Buddhism and dominated by India. It was not until the great masters Wu Daozi, Li Sixun, and Wang Wei emerged in the flourishing Tang dynasty that they revitalized their genius, based it on themselves, and created an independent and great Chinese style of painting. During the Five Dynasties, Song, and Yuan dynasties, talented individuals emerged, and their art reached its peak. However, since the Ming and Qing dynasties, it has steadily declined. The Northern School became the court style, and further declined into rigid and formulaic boundary painting. The Southern School became literati painting, and further declined into the mediocrity of the Four Wangs. In modern times, Western winds have gradually spread eastward, and art has followed. Those who follow the Four Wangs are parochial and cherish their broken brooms. Those who are obsessed with Western painting show off any small achievement, disdaining national traditions. They do not realize that art is the highest expression of the self's spirit and must uphold the spirit of the great masters of the flourishing Tang dynasty, taking the self of this time and place as the center, and the strengths of ancient Europe and the West as the basis, in order to complete the independent personality of Chinese painting."

I have only just begun to glimpse the doorway to painting, but based on the Pavilion owner's views and my own intuition, the advantage of Chinese painting lies in the "comprehensive expression of the combination of real objects and concise impressions." Objects are concrete nature, and impressions are abstract concepts. It begins with observation, continues with editing, and ends with self-expression. The ability of Chinese painting is exhausted. Therefore, Chinese painting initially does not have the divisions of realism, romanticism, and symbolism like Western painting. However, within the six principles of Chinese painting, the spirit of each school is almost entirely included. Speaking of realism, it is not simply copying objects like Western sketching, but observing with the eyes, storing it in the spirit, and when the interest comes, the scene is created with a brush. Speaking of symbolism, it is not simply imagining and writing about a heavenly kingdom, but taking the magnificence of the Five Mountains and comprehensively expressing them on a small canvas. For example, when painting a beauty, one takes the beauty of Xi Shi and Wang Zhaojun and comprehensively expresses it in one person. This kind of expressive technique is not realistic or symbolic, but the comprehensive expression of forging nature. Specifically speaking, like writing about clouds and mountains, the intention is to possess the strengths of each school, making it even more attractive. I observed that the Pavilion owner's realistic and freehand masterpieces were almost all able to utilize their superb skills to develop the inherent spirit of Chinese painting. Even when painting a humble myna bird, he kept ten myna birds and observed their sleeping, eating, flying, and singing postures every day, storing them in his mind. Once the brush and ink arrived, they could exhaust their spirit. If he were to simply take a myna bird and copy it, even if he could obtain the truth of its feathers, it would be difficult to obtain its flying spirit, truly becoming a dead myna bird.

However, Chinese painting is not without shortcomings. Speaking of laws and regulations, it does not have the proportions and perspective of the realist school. Speaking of emotions, it does not have the passionate abandon of the romantic school. Besides this, such as the positive significance of content and the optimistic emotions of color and ink, one must take the strengths of others to make up for one's own weaknesses.

Shenbao Medical Special

Notes on the Unhygienic Conditions of Farmers in Zhenjiang 243

— Zhu Yunda

Understanding from practical work

(1) Farmhouses have poor lighting and ventilation.

(2) Bedrooms have no mosquito nets.

(3) Sewage is dumped everywhere.

(4) Pigsties are built inside the house.

(5) The stove and bedroom are together.

(6) Houses have no windows, stoves have no chimneys.

(7) There are many open-air manure pits.

(8) Garbage is dumped everywhere.

(9) Clothes are not washed or changed for long periods.

(10) Men like to take cold baths, making them susceptible to schistosomiasis.

(11) Women rarely bathe.

(12) Pregnant women often overwork, leading to miscarriages.

(13) During childbirth, they rely on ignorant midwives to mess around, often turning childbirth into death.

(14) They get out of bed to work three days after giving birth.

(15) Infants are poorly nourished and often sick.

(16) There is a superstition in the countryside: if a child is born, they fear it will not grow up, so they specially register its name with a Bodhisattva in a temple. From then on, when the child is sick, they go to the Bodhisattva.

(17) If an infant dies from illness, and the next child born has the same face as the previous one, they believe it is a "debt-collecting ghost"! They will definitely kill it to avoid it collecting more debt. And they believe that if they kill it, they can ensure the next child they raise will be safe?

(18) If an unmarried young man suffers from an illness that cannot be cured for a long time, they implement the so-called "celebratory event to ward off evil," often leading to death.

(19) Early marriage is very common in the countryside.

(20) There are many flies, fleas, and mosquitoes.

(21) The whole family shares a dark, dirty face cloth.

(22) After defecating, they often do not use toilet paper to clean their anus.

(23) They drink raw water, sleep on damp ground, and sleep outdoors.

(24) They boldly eat fermented foods.

(25) They spit and urinate everywhere.

(26) They are greedy for cheapness and buy diseased pork to eat.

(27) They go barefoot and have no habit of wearing socks.

(28) They do not trim their nails.

(29) They drink alcohol and smoke.

(30) When sick, they first endure it, letting it develop naturally. When it seems dangerous, they burn incense and pray to the gods, clutching at straws. If there is no other way, they then seek medical attention.

Waiting for Medicine—Talking about Shasha Medicine Water 244

— Yao Xingshu

The term "waiting for medicine" is not found in records. I remember when I was studying zoology, birds that migrate with the seasons are called migratory birds; insects that are produced in response to the seasons are called seasonal insects. The orioles and swallows herald the coming of spring; the crickets chirp, lamenting the arrival of autumn; external objects show people so deeply, like this.

After finishing my rounds, feeling bored, I leafed through the newspapers and saw advertisements for Ten Drops Water, Shasha Medicine Water, etc., in various colors, catching my eye. Now I know that as the cold goes and the heat comes, the hot summer season is upon us again. The medicine appears according to the season, and the season is made clear by the medicine, so it is called waiting for medicine. Who says it is not appropriate?

There are many names for these types of medicines. For example, let me list them: Baoan Water, Epidemic Crisis Medicine Water, Shen Gong Jizhong Water, Emergency Epidemic Shasha Medicine Water, Jisheng Ten Drops Water, Yixin Water, Duoming Water, Puji Medicine Water, Divine Water, Supreme Saint Water, Emergency Shasha Syndrome Medicine Water, etc., totaling no less than several hundred. Today, the popularity of Ten Drops Water is such that even in remote rural areas, it can be seen. This is because it contains anesthetics and stimulants, easily pleasing people, firstly. The price is low, and the poor can afford it, secondly. Philanthropists do good deeds, purchasing it to distribute, making for powerful promotion, thirdly.

Our people's intelligence is shallow, and they have always followed the crowd, easily susceptible to bewitchment, creating the strange phenomenon of blindly believing in Ten Drops Water today. During the summer and autumn, ordinary people from all levels of society, whenever they feel unwell, have abdominal pain, diarrhea, or other early-stage heat-related illnesses, often call it Shasha, and use it to treat themselves in addition to scraping. If these symptoms disappear after a considerable period, it is attributed to the effect of Ten Drops Water. If it is ineffective, no blame is taken.

The ingredients of these medicines are mostly not produced domestically. After the opening of the seaports, Western medical techniques were introduced to China and came along with it. However, it is impossible to determine who created the formula or when it was manufactured. According to inspection reports, of the 53 types of Shasha Medicine Water examined in Shanghai, about six out of ten contained narcotics and other poisons, and four out of ten did not contain poisons. (See the annual report of the Central Health Laboratory in 1930) In essence, it is nothing more than the following medicines, added, subtracted, or changed.

1. Opium Wine

2. Datura Wine

3. Compound Rhubarb Wine

4. Camphor Wine

5. Capsicum Wine

6. Valerian Wine

7. Peppermint Wine

In terms of medicinal effects, opium wine has the effect of relieving pain and stopping diarrhea, with significant efficacy. The rest are stimulants, cardiotonics, stomachics, and sedatives. This mixture of medicines is more suitable for simple abdominal pain and diarrhea caused by excessive peristalsis (such as those caused by cold stimulation of the abdomen). Those that do not contain narcotics can be used for fainting due to heat, with no objections. As for true cholera, dysentery, acute gastroenteritis, and diarrhea caused by food accumulation, it is harmful and useless to use. Diarrhea is a symptom, not a disease source, and the first priority should be to clear and guide. If the goal is only to stop diarrhea, and an anti-diarrheal containing opium is used in the early stages, it will cause the bacteria to remain in the intestines for a long time, causing great harm. For those with severe and frequent diarrhea, this Ten Drops Water is powerless. Those who are anxious to seek treatment often take excessive amounts, resulting in acute opium poisoning. It is even easier for children to be poisoned because children are more sensitive to opium. There are also those who rely on Shasha Medicine Water and refuse to seek medical treatment immediately, missing the opportunity for treatment, which is even more detrimental.

In short, no matter what kind of Shasha Medicine Water it is, it has no place in medical treatment. Pure doctors do not have this item in their medicine bags or medicine cabinets.

Hongqiao Sanatorium 201 Hongqiao Road Simple Prepared Dean Medical Doctor Ding Huikang Gu Honglie

A Life Equals the Lifespan of One's Blood Vessels 245

— Ding Huikang

In recent years, diseases of the heart and blood vessels have been increasing and have become the most serious national disease. This is because the causes of this disease are numerous and complex, and early recognition of the disease is quite difficult. Furthermore, with the advancement of society and the increasing complexity of human affairs, as well as the growing number of hobbies, all of these factors contribute to the disease developing unconsciously.

The heart is not an independent organ; it is the central point of the entire circulatory system. Therefore, the heart and blood vessels are closely related. Heart disease can originate from diseases of the heart itself, or it can arise from diseases of the blood vessels, such as when the flow of blood encounters resistance that the heart cannot overcome. Consequently, countries around the world are increasingly advancing their research on circulatory and heart diseases, emphasizing both equally.

The increase in heart disease is a common phenomenon, a national and international problem, as Vogl concluded. At the end of the 19th century, in the Bavarian region of Germany, the number of soldiers retiring due to circulatory diseases more than doubled. In the Prussian army, the number of retirees nearly tripled. Similar phenomena occurred in Switzerland. Furthermore, the United States Public Health Service reported a significant increase in heart and kidney diseases since 1892, while the total number of deaths decreased gradually. Of particular note is that in 1931, there were 28 deaths per 10,000 residents due to circulatory diseases, compared to only 21 in 1905. Another startling statistic (from 1931) is as follows:

Out of Every Hundred Deaths

Seven deaths were due to tuberculosis

Ten point nine deaths were due to circulatory diseases

The incidence of these diseases is mostly found between the ages of forty and sixty. Higher-level professionals in large cities are at particularly high risk. For example, among physicians in Vienna, 34.25% suffered from circulatory diseases, while only 15.84% of the general population did. Recently in our country, the deaths of Mr. Hu Zhantang and former院长 Tan (former hospital director Tan) were largely due to circulatory diseases. From what I have seen in magazines and newspapers, deaths due to these diseases are reported almost daily. Therefore, a correct understanding of circulatory diseases and their early diagnosis is not only the greatest effort of our physicians today, but also something that those who generally care about their health should pay attention to, taking precautions before it is too late.

Last spring, I went to Europe to investigate new medicine and visited the Naheim Spa in Germany, the most famous heart sanatorium in all of Europe, where many heads of state and nobles from various countries go to recuperate. The scenery there is beautiful, like a paradise. The establishment of the Heart Research Institute there is particularly world-renowned. The most important tool for studying this disease is the Flek trocardiograph. When the human body is at rest and there are no other muscle movements, only the heart's function generates an electrical current. We guide this current to both ends of the human body and amplify it. The movement passes through an extremely fine filament, and due to the strong electromagnetic force, it oscillates. We use a microscope to magnify the shadow of this movement onto a photographic paper strip, which is what we call an electrocardiogram. We all know that the heart's movement occurs automatically due to a specific stimulus. The center of this stimulus and the nerve conduction pathway run from the atrium to the ventricle. If there is any disruption to this regular movement, whether it is in the front, back, left, or right of the heart, we can use this automatic test to make an accurate diagnosis. However, this machine is not only expensive but also extremely complex in its construction. Even in those countries, only research institutes have this equipment. Given the backwardness of our society's knowledge, it is naturally viewed as mysterious and people are hesitant to try it. In fact, this machine is not only useful for diseases of the heart itself but also for circulatory diseases, such as arteriosclerosis and high blood pressure. Furthermore, symptoms of heart weakness caused by kidney disease, diabetes, acute infectious diseases, lung disease, and alcohol or opium addiction can all be diagnosed using this machine to determine the degree of the condition. Additionally, before performing major surgery or after administering cardiotonic drugs, if one wants to observe the changes in heart function, whether surgery can be performed, and the efficacy of the drugs, this machine is indispensable for such diagnoses. Although my knowledge is limited and I have this equipment, the progress of all research depends on the assistance of my colleagues, which I hope they will be happy to provide.

Common Sense Q&A on Diseases 246

— Cheng Hanzhang

What is acute yellow liver atrophy?

This is a rare disease in which fatty degeneration occurs in the liver parenchyma. Its triggers are syphilis, acute infectious diseases, and poisoning by toxins.

Which infectious diseases can trigger this disease?

Infectious diseases such as typhoid fever, relapsing fever, and smallpox can all trigger this disease.

Which toxins can trigger this disease?

Poisoning by substances such as Salvarsan, 606, 914, and poisonous mushrooms can trigger this condition. Does the occurrence of acute yellow liver atrophy relate to gender or age?

It mostly affects pregnant women and postpartum women between the ages of thirty and forty.

What are the symptoms of this disease?

The symptoms can be divided into two stages.

What are the symptoms of the first stage?

The symptoms of the first stage are gastrointestinal symptoms, such as loss of appetite, nausea, vomiting, and stomach pain. Pain in the liver area, followed by jaundice. This stage usually lasts from a few days to two weeks.

What are the symptoms of the second stage?

The symptoms of the second stage are severe neurological symptoms, including severe headaches, restlessness, insomnia, delirium, convulsions, drowsiness, and coma. At the same time, the liver shrinks, and after several days, it shrinks to half or a quarter of its normal size. The spleen, however, is often enlarged. Severe jaundice also develops, and bleeding is seen in the skin, mucous membranes, gastrointestinal tract, uterus, etc.

Are there changes in the patient's urine?

The urine contains bile pigments and bile fluids, the amount of urea decreases, and sometimes a small amount of protein is seen. It contains specific Leucin and Tyrosin.

Are there changes in the stool?

The stool is constipated and clay-like. The pulse is rapid, ranging from 120 to 140 beats per minute.

How much higher than normal is the patient's body temperature during this period?

Most patients develop a moderate fever. Before death, the temperature rises to 39 or 40 degrees Celsius.

What changes occur in the patient's blood?

The number of red blood cells in the blood increases, and the hemoglobin rises. The number of white blood cells also increases.

How is this disease diagnosed?

Early diagnosis is very difficult. It should be differentiated from duodenal jaundice, acute phosphorus poisoning, and Wilson's disease.

What is the prognosis?

Absolutely poor. It is invariably fatal within two to three weeks of onset.

How is acute yellow liver atrophy treated?

Only insulin and glucose injections are used. If syphilis is present, anti-syphilitic treatment can be administered. (End)
