Domestic Medicinal Plants (Continued) 247

— Zhou Mengbai

Pedaliaceae (Sesame Family)

Sesamum indicum L. (Sesame)

(Plant) Native to India and Egypt, cultivated in gardens, an annual herb. Stems are quadrangular, up to 1 meter tall, densely covered with short hairs. Leaves are opposite, petiolate, oblong or lanceolate, edges wavy, apex acute. Lower leaves often trifoliate. In summer, small white or light purple flowers bloom from the leaf axils; corolla tubular, 5-lobed. Capsules cylindrical, containing black or white seeds.

(Raw Drug) Sesame Seed (Semen Sesami) is collected from the mature seeds. The seeds are oval, tapering at one end, slightly flattened, 3-4 mm long, 1-1.5 mm thick, surface black or white, with a mild oily taste.

(Constituents) Seeds contain 45-55% fatty oil. Fatty acid composition (%) of sesame oil is as follows:

Oleic acid 48.1 Linolsaure 36.8 Palmitinsaure 7.7

Stearinsaure 4.6 Arachinsaure 0.4 Lignocerinsaure 0.04

(Medicinal Use) Sesame Oil (Oleum Sesami) can be used as a base for ointments. It can be used to prepare ammonia liniment, camphor ointment, simple ointment, etc.

(Other Uses) Used as edible oil and for manufacturing artificial butter.

Bignoniaceae (Trumpet Creeper Family)

Catalpa ovate, G. Don (O. KAempferi, Siebet Zucc.) (Chinese Catalpa)

(Plant) Native to China, can be cultivated everywhere, a deciduous tree. Leaves long-petiolate, broadly heart-shaped, edges generally wavy, often deeply lobed, apex acute, glabrous on the underside. Pale yellow bell-shaped flowers bloom in early summer. Capsules narrow and linear.

American Catalpa (C. bignonioides, Walt), native to North America, similar to the previous species, underside of leaves densely covered with soft hairs, flowers white, capsules shorter and larger than the previous species.

Catalpa wood is of excellent quality, traditionally known as the "King of Woods." Annotation in the Compendium of Materia Medica states: "Catalpa is the leader of all trees, hence it is called the King of Woods." Its wood is of superior quality, unmatched by any other. The characters carved on woodblocks are called zi, and the emperor's coffin is called zigong, because it is a good material. There is a popular saying that planting this tree can prevent lightning strikes. Luo Yuan's Erya Yi states, "If this tree is in the house, the other materials will not be struck by lightning."

(Raw Drug) Catalpa Fruit (Fructus Cotalpae), collected from the fruits. The fruits are narrow and linear, about 40 cm long, about 0.5 cm wide, often splitting along the ventral suture. Surface dark brown, texture rough and easily broken, containing many seeds. Seeds wing-shaped, seed coat with many hairs, easily dispersed. Taste slightly astringent.

(Constituents) Fruits contain citric acid and its alkali salts. The diuretic effect of this raw drug is partly attributed to these substances. Its aqueous extract (Extractum) contains 14.16% ash, most of which is alkali salts (K 23-27% in the ash).

(Medicinal Use) Old accounts: Catalpa fruit has a significant diuretic effect.

Prescription Example: Catalpa Fruit Decoction, used to treat edema.

Catalpa Fruit (6.0) 200.

Administer above dose in three divided doses per day.

Scrophulariaceae (Figwort Family)

Rehmannia glutinosa Mhosch arw purpurea, Makino (Chinese Foxglove)

(Plant) Native to China, can be cultivated everywhere, a perennial herb. Stems up to 30 cm tall, whole plant densely covered with short hairs. Root leaves basal, stem leaves alternate, petiolate, oblong, edges uneven, serrated with blunt tips, surface wrinkled. Terminal raceme, with red labiate flowers blooming in early summer.

White-Flowered Rehmannia (R. glutinosa, Libosch, var, lutea, Makino). Shape smaller than the previous species, leaves generally basal, flowers pale yellowish-white.

(Cultivation Method) On a sloping hillside, create longitudinal strips, one foot apart, with five-inch drainage ditches between them. In late June, divide the roots stored from the previous year into one-inch pieces, plant each piece three inches apart. Fertilizers include bean cake, basal fertilizer, etc. Harvest the roots from late November to January, brush off the soil, dry them, and store them in sand. Each mu (unit of area) yields approximately 200 jin (unit of weight) of fresh roots.

(Raw Drug) Rehmannia Root (Rhizoma Rehmanniae), collected from the rhizomes of the above two species. White-flowered rehmannia is difficult to cultivate and easily rots during storage, so usually only the species with crimson flowers is planted. Rehmannia exists in three forms: dried rehmannia, fresh rehmannia, and prepared rehmannia.

Dried Rehmannia: Collected in winter, dried under the sun. Surface grayish-white or grayish-brown, longitudinally and transversely wrinkled, with warty protuberances, irregularly curved, approximately one centimeter thick. Cross-section smooth, dark purple, texture soft. The drug is odorless, has a sweet taste, slightly bitter.

Examining the cross-section under a microscope reveals the integument, formed by several layers of integument cells, forming a covering tissue. The cells of the cortical parenchyma often contain yellow resinous material. Stone cells are extremely rare. Vascular bundles arranged in a single row, rarely in two rows, accompanied by false vascular bundles, arranged radially.

Fresh Rehmannia: Collected and stored in shady sandy soil. The surface is yellowish-red, and the larger, moister pieces are of better quality.

Prepared Rehmannia: Fresh rehmannia that has been steamed and dried. The blacker the surface, the better the quality.

(Constituents) Roots contain mannitol and sugars.

(Medicinal Use) Old accounts: Rehmannia is a blood-tonifying and strengthening drug, especially valued for treating consumptive weakness. It also has a hemostatic effect, treating hemoptysis, epistaxis, hematemesis, uterine bleeding, etc. Daily dose is 5-10 cm, in decoction. The juice of fresh rehmannia can be applied to wounds.

"Cools the blood, generates blood, tonifies kidney yin, removes dryness of the skin, eliminates various damp-heat conditions."

Prescription Example: Tang-kuei and Six-Yellow Decoction, for general weakness, especially for consumptive patients with night sweats.

Tang-kuei (Angelica sinensis) · Astragalus, 4.0 each; Yellow Leaves (Rehmannia glutinosae folium) · Scutellaria (Scutellaria baicalensis) · Coptis (Coptis chinensis) · Fresh Rehmannia · Prepared Rehmannia, 3.0 each.

Prepare as a decoction (200), administer in three divided doses per day.

Common Sense Q&A on Teeth (35) 248

— Lin Jianxian

Chapter VII: Treatment of Dental Diseases

(Question 175) How is chronic infectious periodontitis treated?

Answer: This is chronic alveolar abscess, which can be divided into those with and without fistulas. First, the pulp chamber should be opened, the apical foramen enlarged, and pus drained with a probe. Cotton soaked in disinfectant is sealed into the root canal, and the dressing is changed daily until the pus is completely drained and there is no odor. Then, the root canal is filled. If the abscess has formed a fistula, the medicine solution can be injected from the pulp chamber, flowing out from the fistula to wash away the pus and dirt. A corrosive agent can be used to eliminate the fistula. In addition, there is a surgical treatment method, in which the alveolar bone is broken open, the tip of the root is cut off, and the abscess is scraped away to seek a radical cure.

(Question 176) Can the affected tooth be retained when suffering from acute or chronic alveolar abscess?

Answer: The various treatments mentioned above are very complicated and the results are difficult to stabilize. Often, prolonged treatment is still futile. This is because the pus-causing bacteria are deeply hidden in the affected area at the end of the root, making it difficult to completely eradicate. Therefore, if the treatment is ineffective, or the tooth is defective and useless, or if there are complications, the affected tooth should be extracted. Forcing its retention will only increase suffering. However, unless there are special circumstances, it is not advisable to extract the tooth while the acute symptoms have not subsided.

Section IV: On the Treatment of Alveolar Pyorrhea

(Question 177) How is early-stage alveolar pyorrhea treated?

Answer: Use special instruments to scrape away the calculus, then apply a suitable astringent to the gums several times, and frequently rinse with mouthwash.

(Question 178) How is alveolar pyorrhea with pus pockets treated?

Answer: First, thoroughly wash and scrape clean all the calculus and pus in the pus pockets, and apply an astringent. For stubborn cases, a corrosive agent must be used to destroy the affected area. If drug treatment is ineffective, surgery can be used to remove the pus pockets. If all methods are ineffective, the affected tooth must be extracted to prevent it from infecting adjacent teeth. In addition to local application of drugs, there are also oral medications and injections, which can sometimes have remarkable effects.

(Question 179) How are teeth that have already become loose treated?

Answer: Appliances can be used to secure and stabilize the teeth. After the disease subsides, or it may be possible to restore the original stability.

(Question 180) How is alveolar pyorrhea caused by systemic conditions treated?

Answer: First, treat the underlying cause, such as diabetes and venereal disease. As for the surgery and medications required for local treatment, they are the same as described above. However, these conditions should be treated by both dentists and general practitioners, which will be more effective.

(Question 181) Why should patients with general alveolar pyorrhea patiently cooperate with the dentist?

Answer: Because this condition requires long-term treatment, if the patient cannot cooperate closely with the doctor and follow his guidance, even if there is an excellent treatment method, a permanent effect cannot be obtained.

(Question 182) What hygiene measures should patients pay attention to themselves?

Answer: Avoid constipation, drink more water, and eat more fruits, vegetables, and brown rice to increase gastrointestinal activity. Do not swallow any pus in the mouth. Rinse your mouth immediately after eating. Get plenty of sunlight and fresh air. Avoid excessive indulgence and overwork, but appropriate exercise is very beneficial.

Section V: On the Treatment of Toothache

(Question 183) How do we feel toothache?

Answer: Because there is a problem with the teeth or other parts. The trigeminal nerve, which is distributed in the teeth, is stimulated, so it feels pain. Therefore, toothache cannot be considered an independent disease; it is just a warning indicating the existence of disease, so that we can quickly go to the doctor.

How to Suppress Smuggling 249

— Zibin

The Shanghai Municipal All Circles Anti-Smuggling Association was established recently. Regarding their position and work, it is clearly stated in the declaration: "...Hoping to assist the government from the perspective of automatic public participation, reporting smuggled goods, sanctioning traitors, to maintain the nation's economic lifeline, hoping that compatriots across the country will rise up together to eliminate smuggling...".

The prohibition of smuggled goods, apart from traitors, is fervently advocated by compatriots across the country. However, how should it be prohibited? Although the Anti-Smuggling Association has proposed two principles: "Report smuggled goods, sanction traitors," and has also appointed several people to draft an organizational outline and work outline, we cannot help but doubt whether such vague regulations and generalized methods can be effective in practice!

Because, the enemy's conspiracies are progressing day by day. They have torn off their hypocritical masks and use force to protect smuggling. It is precisely because of this that we feel that the old methods are no longer sufficient to deal with the current environment. Moreover, how can we talk about conscience to traitors who only care about profit, and how can the people thoroughly recognize smuggled goods besides贪便宜 (greed for cheapness)?

Therefore, I feel that the so-called "reporting smuggled goods, sanctioning traitors" is perhaps too simplistic a view of the matter.

However, should we retreat in the face of difficulty? Of course not! I agree with the proposition of "reporting smuggled goods, sanctioning traitors," and I dare to believe that every Chinese citizen also agrees with this proposition. Precisely because we agree with this proposition, we must make our proposition a reality, we must use force to stop smuggling!

At present, only the use of force can stop smuggling!

While discussing how to suppress smuggling, I also thought about the forced ban of the plays "Smuggling" by the Experimental Little Theater and the Ant Troupe. In the territory of China, dramas depicting the reality of the Japanese "smuggling" within China are unable to be staged. Then, I do not know if the existence of China is still recognized in other countries of the world? Now, although some people have requested the Taxpaying Chinese Association to make a serious protest to the Municipal Council, for the sake of support, the Anti-Smuggling Association should take the lead and strive for it. Otherwise, if dramas depicting the reality of "smuggling" cannot be staged, how much less so will it be to "report smuggled goods, sanction traitors"!

Reading "Ten Records of a Southern Journey" (Part 2) 250

— Taisheng

Now let's excerpt a few paragraphs to take a look:

In the seventh record, "Mountain, Water, Bridge and Tunnel," the author writes about the railway project along the Hunan-Guangdong Highway. Here is a passage with beautiful writing:

"The hand-cranked vehicle was placed on the rails, and Engineer Zhang and us, proceeded in the mountains that were artificially cut open. The mountains are ochre red, the stones are of all sizes and shapes, like snails, like millstones, like lions and dogs... As for what we saw on both sides, above were layers upon layers of continuous mountain peaks, and below was winding, long-flowing turquoise water, the mountains turned with the water, the water flowed around the mountains, the scenery was beautiful, as if in a painting..."

In the eighth record, "Guangzhou's Famous Sites," Guangzhou is described very clearly. The author went to Yuexiu Mountain to visit the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall, then went to Huanghuagang to commemorate the "Seventy-Two Martyrs Tomb," and lingered for a long time at the Memorial Monument to the Soldiers of the 19th Route Army. The author also mentions the British and French concessions in Shamian, Guangzhou. The author says:

"...It is said that this Shamian concession has no lease term and no lease treaty. The Westerners still pay a few hundred dollars in rent every year. From this point, we cannot help but deeply lament the diplomacy handled by the previous government. Remembering the Shaji Massacre of that year, passing through the current June 23rd Road, the pain in my heart goes without saying." These words are said with great sorrow.

The ninth record is "Macau Zhongshan." On the afternoon of March 12, the author took a Hong Kong-Guangdong-Macau steamer from Hong Kong to Macau.

Macau, under the Portuguese policy of opium, gambling, and drugs, has caused the Chinese people of Macau to be forever mired in this bottomless pit. Therefore, when the author walked into a Macau hotel, he wrote:

"...When the elevator stopped and I stepped onto the second floor, a smell of opium smoke rushed straight into my nostrils. Under the short doors of each room, one could glimpse the four legs of a man and a woman, placed horizontally on two square stools. Undoubtedly, they were lying on the bed heavily smoking their opium. In addition, the sound of playing cards, clattering, the sound of talking, giggling, dozens of rooms, not one was empty."

In fact, we know that hotels in the Shanghai concessions are no different.

In addition, Macau has large-scale casinos, I do not know how many. These are all the most ruthless policies of the Portuguese to deal with the Chinese. Therefore, the author finally wrote!

"Although the Portuguese use opium and gambling policies to extract money from the Chinese, in recent years, the whole world has suffered from the invasion of depression, how can Macau not be affected? The income from opium and gambling is now decreasing year by year. The Portuguese have no other choice but to cleverly establish new items to levy taxes. For example, electricity must also be taxed, everything must be taxed, but the result is still insufficient. The future of Macau, under such circumstances, is always uneasy for the Portuguese." This passage is a true and accurate exposure of the Portuguese in Macau.

Outside of Macau, the author also went to Zhongshan to visit Sun Yat-sen's former residence.

The last chapter is the tenth record, "Hong Kong Tourism." Here, the author narrates the simple history of Hong Kong and Kowloon being leased to the British. In addition to visiting Hong Kong, Kowloon, Repulse Bay, and the aerial tram, the author further points out the recession in the Hong Kong market and the market being filled with Japanese goods.

Hong Kong is beautiful, especially the area around Repulse Bay beach. The author almost used the tone of poetry to eulogize Repulse Bay: Let's see:

"I love Repulse Bay the most! On the veranda of the Repulse Bay Hotel, looking at the clear, mirror-like seawater and the azure sky, all around is quiet, without a sound, the whole soul is in the embrace of the blue sea and the green sky. Especially the vast lawn in front of the hotel, so green that it is enchanting; in the northeast corner there is a flower shed, covered with bunches of yellow flowers, everywhere showing a strong spring light..."

Regarding the "Hanyu Records of Travel" appended at the end, due to the limited space, it is omitted.

Flower Drum Opera (Continued) 251

— Shadow Dull

Roughly speaking, performing a day of flower drum opera, including food and lodging, only costs about ten dollars, so it's easily affordable. When performing flower drum opera, they would use straw mats and wooden boards in the village square to build a stage. They would perform two shows daily, one during the day and one at night. For the night show, they would hang two bamboo baskets upside down on the stage, line them with mud, and place two large kerosene lamps inside, one on the left and one on the right. Because the wicks were thick, even strong winds wouldn't extinguish them.

When a certain village was performing flower drum opera, people from far and near would rush to see it upon hearing the news, even those from more than ten miles away. Moreover, because people had less to do at night and were relatively free, the audience was quite lively. On a moonlit night...

Page 22

...in a village draped in a layer of black, a stage corner was brightly lit with lamps and candles, and a flower drum opera was being performed. The audience stood quietly listening, which was, of course, absolutely different from the atmosphere inside a Shanghai theater, and possessed a different, more common touch.

When a flower drum opera was performed, a "Yang Tune Performance" was usually performed before the main play. The so-called "Yang Tune Performance" was like ballad singers singing a "double opening" before the main story. Although some plays in the flower drum opera repertoire had four or five, or even seven or eight characters on stage, most of them were duets between male and female roles. The male role was even called "Westerner" by the villagers. We don't know the meaning of this term.

Most of the people who sang flower drum opera were self-taught. The interludes played on the huqin (Chinese violin) formed their own unique melody. Originally, there was no formal musical score, and most flower drum opera plays were passed down orally, without scripts. The actors could make slight changes according to their own improvisation without being restricted. However, the lyrics were rhymed, and they paid close attention to the rhymes.

About twenty years ago, all the female roles were played by men in disguise. It wasn't until later that women learned to sing flower drum opera, and from then on, all female roles in flower drum opera could be played by women. However, in incomplete troupes, the female roles were still played by men. After the rise of amusement parks in Shanghai, flower drum opera troupes were recruited and given the euphemistic name "Shen Opera." It is said that the place of origin of flower drum opera was indeed near Shanghai, such as the areas of Pudong and Qibao, so calling it "Shen Opera" can be said to be appropriate. Some people in our villages call flower drum opera "Eastern Township Tune" for this reason. Even people from the Western Township who sing flower drum opera have to learn the Eastern Township accent.

Many of the plays in the flower drum opera repertoire are quite obscene, but there are also some better ones. It's just because the people in the countryside, like the people of Shanghai who like to watch Bai Yushuang's "Widow Ma's Shop," always welcome low-brow scripts, so they mostly want to sing obscene lyrics and vulgar tunes. As a result, the authorities considered flower drum opera to be detrimental to public morals and banned it. In fact, if flower drum opera could be improved, removing obscene plays and specializing in plays that arouse the rural masses, I think it would be the most genuine and great driving force of popular drama in the vicinity of Shanghai.

Sea Burial Song 252

— Zhu Lu

The sea howls.

In the sea breeze, a woman paced back and forth with faltering steps. The sea breeze scattered her long hair and made her clothes rustle. The woman's face was strangely pale, and her bare feet stepped over the piled-up broken shells.

The seawater surges.

Her footsteps fell on the sand, step by step, leaving sunken footprints on the sand. She welcomed the gale, walking on the beach.

She walked madly, letting the seawater rush over and hit her toes. Her eyes stared blankly at the sea, filled with anger and resentment.

The tide is rising.

Her face twitched, her mouth opened wide, letting the sea breeze pour into her throat, causing her to hiccup violently. Her hair was disheveled like a wild ghost, her hands clenched convulsively, and her head rushed into the wind.

She screamed madly on the ground, her voice so miserable.

Her feet danced on the beach, and the seawater splashed up.

Her eyes stared blankly at the rolling sea, as if through the sea, shooting into the dark place. The sea in front of her seemed to fade away, showing swollen corpses one by one.

Past memories emerged one after another.

She thought sadly and angrily that the sea had buried three generations of her family.

When she was still a child, the sea took away her father. When she grew up, the sea took away her husband. Ten years passed, and yesterday the sea buried her only child.

The sea took away her happiness, the sea snatched away her beloved ones one by one from her arms, the sea submerged all her hopes. She thought crazily on the ground, her eyes overflowing with hot tears.

She had hated the sea since she was a child.

She remembered that when she was young, she was picking up seashells. The blow of her father being buried at sea ended her quiet childhood. She was sent to another fisherman. When she grew up and got married and was about to regain happiness, the sea took away her husband and her fishing boat. She lived a hard life until ten years later, when she placed her last hope of happiness on her handsome child. On a stormy day, the sea swallowed her son again – the sea buried three generations of her family.

The heavy taxes and the piling debts made her dear ones leave her embrace and throw themselves into the sea, to be buried at sea. They were all young and had excellent hopes. They grew from the earth, but one by one they were swallowed by the sea.

They all knew that the sea was dangerous. They were whipped by poverty in the sea to find a way to live, and one by one became prisoners of the sea.

She remembered yesterday, when her child sailed out on the sailboat, she still saw his face full of youthful radiance and his strong body. She secretly prayed for him, "May he return safely!"

Attacked by a big storm, her child would not return. The sea cruelly robbed her of everything.

She had given her beloved ones to the sea, but the sea brought and gave her – some broken planks, clothes, and scattered things that floated from the sea.

She was angry, her eyes hostile to the seawater.

The sea roared, the seawater soaked her knees, the rolling water rose, and the waves surged.

She angrily stretched out her fists and threw herself into the sea. She was rushing wildly in the tide.

Her feet sank in, she struggled, sinking deeper, her body shaking, and a wave of tide shook her.

She roared desperately, the roar was so tragic and sharp, containing generations of anger and a lifetime of resentment.

The seawater submerged her chest...

The tide surged like boiling.

Tiger Plague 253

— Lu Fu

Rural Life Accelerates – One of the Greens

It is said that this year is the "Year of the Tiger Plague."

Tiger Plague is a new academic name, commonly known as cholera, and called "plague" by the common people. They also say that it is a disaster caused by the wrath of the Plague God, so in the villages and towns of North China, you can often see temples to the Plague God.

Because the general farmers know that the plague is caused by the wrath of the Plague God, naturally those who get the plague should burn incense and paper, build altars and set up rituals, hoping that the Plague God will show great compassion and be able to calm his anger and turn misfortune into good fortune, and have to submit to the Plague God.

In the autumn of the 21st year of the Republic of China, when the plague was advancing towards Jinan along the Jiaoji Railway, I was a primary school teacher in a small county in Jiaodong, forty or fifty miles away from the Jiaoji Railway, in a small town more than ten miles away from the county seat. The people in the whole town were worried about the arrival of the Plague God, and every household burned incense and paper. The fragrance and ashes of paper filled the sky above the whole town.

The training director of the primary school was an extremely anti-superstitious person. Every time he taught a class, he always took some time to discuss the issue of the plague. He also specially organized a propaganda team to break superstition, divided into groups and set off to explain the prevention and treatment of the plague to the farmers in the whole town. The most effective method was naturally vaccination, but at that time there was no such facility in the town. In order to prevent the occurrence of the plague, although there was a lack of equipment on the active side, on the passive side, the township office immediately stopped the business of meat merchants and prohibited eating raw cooked vegetables and raw water. That was the late summer when watermelons were out of season.

The Plague God did not reduce his murderous aura because of burning incense and paper. More than two-thirds of the villages in the whole county had already fallen into his clutches! The first person in this small town was a young strong man who died suddenly in the field while working! That night, everyone in the town knew the shocking news. The smoke of incense, the ashes of paper, and the sound of firecrackers added to the atmosphere. The whole town was unusually lively that night.

In the primary school, because it was just the beginning of the semester, most of the students from other villages could not come because of the plague, so there were very few people. Only half of them were students from this town. When a primary school student came crying to ask for leave, another student also came crying to ask for leave. One reported that his mother had died! One reported that his father had died! The next morning, the primary school student who asked for leave also died! The plague killed people in twenty-odd hours if slow, and quickly if it was fatal where the person died after falling to the ground with their legs twitching out. Moreover, the person was unconscious when they got sick, and it was very difficult to take medicine. The most convenient way was still acupuncture. The only old scholar and traditional Chinese medicine doctor in this small town could only prescribe decoctions, but did not know acupuncture. Therefore, those who got sick and sought medical treatment had to go to other villages. A family who got the plague sent someone to another village to invite an acupuncture doctor. It happened that the doctor was treating a family who got the plague. Not only did he not cure the patient's disease, he fell under the bed and died! The person who invited the doctor not only did not bring the doctor back, but died in the doctor's home. The person who carried the coffin of the sick person in the morning was carried by others himself at night. The whole town echoed with tragic cries, and the streets were filled with children running around in mourning clothes. Every day, when dusk was dim, the sound of firecrackers was mixed with the mournful and prolonged tune of "calling the soul." The weather was as sultry as a whole piece, and in the firelight of burning the clothes of the dead, the hot wind of summer steamed up with a fishy smell.

In the northern rural custom of funerals, there is a program of "breaking tiles," which is to break new tiles in front of the coffin during the funeral. Because the school was repairing the classroom, people with tears in their eyes were constantly coming in and out to borrow tiles every afternoon. The school's tiles were constantly being borrowed every day, and people's lives were constantly being destroyed by the Plague God! When the sound of crying came from the school's northern neighbor, we were so frightened that we moved to the front yard. The front neighbor sent the sound of crying again; everyone moved to the middle again, and when the sound of crying came from all the neighbors, the school had to be forced to close! Of course, because the teachers could not settle down to teach, and the students were also slowly decreasing.

According to the village elders, "The Plague God is particular about the year, and it will be better when the year turns over." The whole town then decided on the day of "New Year" on the desperate road where there was no way to think. Whether rich or poor, they were all waving the sweat of summer to prepare for "New Year." On the morning of that day, which was full of "New Year" scenes, the training director who opposed superstition and the Plague God and I were frightened and left that small town.

On the road from the town to the county seat, in every village, on the streets, children running around in mourning clothes, everyone was pulling a sad face, and everywhere we heard cries, the sound of firecrackers, and the mournful and prolonged sound of "calling the soul." A gust of hot wind blew the smell of incense and the smell of burning paper. Several villages had run clean, quietly leaving behind a pile of broken houses that could not be taken away.

When I saw the news of "Year of the Tiger Plague" in the newspaper, a tragic picture of the plague wreaking havoc, the sincere faces of a group of farmers who had to believe in the Plague God, and a pair of pitiful eyes clearly appeared before my eyes again.

Ballad Singing 255

He Yunfang He Qinfang Double Pearl Ball Chinese and Western (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening Chapter "Gold and Beauty"

What in the world is easy to move people's hearts? Only gold and beauty. Gold can take away the ambition of the common man. A word from a beauty is like an imperial edict. Look at how many young people have suffered setbacks. It is also for gold and beauty. I remember that King Xiang of Chu, a hero, committed suicide at Wujiang. He was reluctant to leave Beauty Yu. Look at how corrupt officials fight for power. They are always thinking about gold. Some are for gold, brothers fighting with each other. Some are for gold, plotting money and harming lives. Some are for gold, loved ones become enemies. Some are for gold, husband and wife separated in two places. Some are for gold, conscience changes in an instant. Some are for gold, losing virtue and losing themselves. Gold, I think you are, an evil doing supreme power. I don't know how many people you have harmed. I see you. You have great power to reverse right and wrong. So, gold can buy the heart of a beauty. Let's see, since ancient times, beauties have had great magic power. Not only can they topple kingdoms and cities. I remember that Tang Jieyuan in Xiao Yuan. He was full of affection for the beauty. Wen Bizheng in Double Pearl Phoenix. He sold himself to the Heavenly Official's door. Like a scholar, he doesn't want to do it.
